### Sector composition {#Sector_composition}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Sector composition")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg/220px-Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sanlitun_at_dusk.jpg) The [Taikoo Li Sanlitun](/wiki/Taikoo_Li_Sanlitun "Taikoo Li Sanlitun") shopping arcade is a destination for locals and visitors.

The city has a [post-industrial economy](/wiki/Post-industrial_economy "Post-industrial economy") that is dominated by the [tertiary sector](/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy "Tertiary sector of the economy") (services), which generated 83.8% of output, followed by the [secondary sector](/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy "Secondary sector of the economy") (manufacturing, construction) at 15.8% and the [primary sector](/wiki/Primary_sector "Primary sector") (agriculture, mining) at 0.26%.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^ The services sector is broadly diversified with professional services, wholesale and retail, information technology, commercial real estate, scientific research, and residential real estate each contributing at least 6% to the city's economy in 2022.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^{#cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_158-0}

The single largest sub-sector remains industry, whose share of overall output has shrunk to 12.1% in 2022.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^ The mix of industrial output has changed significantly since 2010 when the city announced that 140 highly-polluting, energy and water resource intensive enterprises would be relocated from the city in five years.^[\[153\]](#cite_note-159)^ The relocation of [Capital Steel](/wiki/Shougang_Corporation "Shougang Corporation") to neighboring Hebei province had begun in 2005.^[\[154\]](#cite_note-160)^^[\[155\]](#cite_note-161)^ In 2013, output of automobiles, aerospace products, [semiconductors](/wiki/Semiconductor "Semiconductor"), pharmaceuticals, and food processing all increased.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^{#cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_158-1}

In the farmland around Beijing, vegetables and fruits have displaced grain as the primary crops under cultivation.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^ In 2013, the tonnage of vegetable, edible fungus and fruit harvested was over three times that of grain.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^ In 2013, overall acreage under cultivation shrank along with most categories of produce as more land was reforested for environmental reasons.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^{#cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_158-4}  

### Economic zones {#Economic_zones}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Economic zones")\]  
For a more comprehensive list, see [List of economic and technological development zones in Beijing](/wiki/List_of_economic_and_technological_development_zones_in_Beijing "List of economic and technological development zones in Beijing").
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Parkview_Green_and_CBD_skyline_%2820210927131419%29.jpg/220px-Parkview_Green_and_CBD_skyline_%2820210927131419%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Parkview_Green_and_CBD_skyline_(20210927131419).jpg) The skyline of [Beijing CBD](/wiki/Beijing_CBD "Beijing CBD") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Zhongguancun_from_Huangzhuang_North_Footbridge_%2820201214122926%29.jpg/220px-Zhongguancun_from_Huangzhuang_North_Footbridge_%2820201214122926%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Zhongguancun_from_Huangzhuang_North_Footbridge_(20201214122926).jpg) [Zhongguancun](/wiki/Zhongguancun "Zhongguancun") is a technology hub in [Haidian District](/wiki/Haidian_District "Haidian District").

In 2006, the city government identified six high-end economic output zones around Beijing as the primary engines for local economic growth. In 2012, the six zones produced 43.3% of the city's GDP, up from 36.5% in 2007.^[\[156\]](#cite_note-162)^^[\[157\]](#cite_note-163)^ The six zones are:{#cite_ref-163}

1. [Zhongguancun](/wiki/Zhongguancun "Zhongguancun"), China's silicon village in Haidian District northwest of the city, is home to both established and start-up tech companies. In the first two quarters of 2014, 9,895 companies registered in the six zones, among which 6,150 were based in Zhongguancun.^[\[158\]](#cite_note-164)^ Zhongguancun is also the center of [Beijing-Tianjin-Shijiazhuang Hi-Tech Industrial Belt](/wiki/Beijing-Tianjin-Shijiazhuang_Hi-Tech_Industrial_Belt "Beijing-Tianjin-Shijiazhuang Hi-Tech Industrial Belt").{#cite_ref-164}
2. [Beijing Financial Street](/wiki/Beijing_Financial_Street "Beijing Financial Street"), in Xicheng District on the west side of the city between Fuxingmen and Fuchengmen, is lined with headquarters of large state banks and insurance companies. The country's financial regulatory agencies including the [central bank](/wiki/People%27s_Bank_of_China "People's Bank of China"), [bank regulator](/wiki/China_Banking_Regulatory_Commission "China Banking Regulatory Commission"), [securities regulator](/wiki/China_Securities_Regulatory_Commission "China Securities Regulatory Commission"), and [foreign exchange authority](/wiki/State_Administration_of_Foreign_Exchange "State Administration of Foreign Exchange") are located in the neighborhood.
3. [Beijing Central Business District (CBD)](/wiki/Beijing_CBD "Beijing CBD"), is actually located to the east of downtown, near the embassies along the eastern Third Ring Road between Jianguomenwai and Chaoyangmenwai. The CBD is home to most of the [city's skyscraper office buildings](/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Beijing "List of tallest buildings in Beijing"). Most of the city's foreign companies and professional service firms are based in the CBD.
4. [Beijing Economic and Technological Development Area](/wiki/Beijing_Economic_and_Technological_Development_Area "Beijing Economic and Technological Development Area"), better known as [Yizhuang](/wiki/Yizhuang,_Beijing "Yizhuang, Beijing"), is an industrial park the straddles the southern Fifth Ring Road in Daxing District. It has attracted pharmaceutical, information technology, and materials engineering companies.^[\[159\]](#cite_note-social_economic-165)^{#cite_ref-social_economic_165-0}
5. Beijing Airport Economic Zone was created in 1993 and surrounds the [Beijing Capital International Airport](/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport "Beijing Capital International Airport") in Shunyi District northeast of the city. In addition to logistics, airline services, and trading firms, this zone is also home to Beijing's automobile assembly plants.
6. Beijing Olympic Center Zone surrounds the [Olympic Green](/wiki/Olympic_Green "Olympic Green") due north of downtown and is developing into an entertainment, sports, tourism and business convention center.

[Shijingshan](/wiki/Shijingshan "Shijingshan"), on the western outskirts of the city, is a traditional heavy industrial base for steel-making.^[\[160\]](#cite_note-166)^ Chemical plants are concentrated in the far eastern suburbs.{#cite_ref-166}

Less legitimate enterprises also exist. Urban Beijing is known for being a center of [infringed](/wiki/Copyright_infringement "Copyright infringement") goods; anything from the latest designer clothing to DVDs can be found in markets all over the city, often marketed to expatriates and international visitors.^[\[161\]](#cite_note-167)^{#cite_ref-167}  

Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Demographics")\]  
Main article: [Demographics of Beijing](/wiki/Demographics_of_Beijing "Demographics of Beijing")
{#cite_ref-BeijingHistoricalGDP_156-1}

|                         Year                         |            |        |
|                         1953                         | 2,768,149  |  ---   |
|                         1964                         | 7,568,495  | +9.57% |
|                         1982                         | 9,230,687  | +1.11% |
|                         1990                         | 10,819,407 | +2.00% |
|                         2000                         | 13,569,194 | +2.29% |
|                         2010                         | 19,612,368 | +3.75% |
| 2020^[\[150\]](#cite_note-BeijingHistoricalGDP-156)^ | 21,893,095 | +1.11% |
|------------------------------------------------------|------------|--------|
| Population size may be affected by changes on administrative divisions.  |||
[Historical population]

In 2021, Beijing had a total population of 21.89 million within the municipality, of which 19.16 million (87.5 percent) resided in urban districts or suburban townships and 2.73 million (12.5) lived in rural villages.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^ The encompassing [metropolitan area](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area") was estimated by the [OECD](/wiki/OECD "OECD") (Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development) to have, as of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit)^, a population of 24.9 million.^[\[162\]](#cite_note-168)^^[\[163\]](#cite_note-oecd2015-169)^{#cite_ref-oecd2015_169-0}

Within China, the city ranked [second in urban population](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_China_by_population "List of cities in China by population") after Shanghai and the [third in municipal population](/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipalities_of_China "Direct-controlled municipalities of China") after Shanghai and Chongqing. Beijing also ranks among the most populous cities in the world, a distinction the city has held for much of the past 800 years, especially during the 15th to early 19th centuries when it was [the largest city in the world](/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_throughout_history "List of largest cities throughout history").

About 13 million of the city's residents in 2013 had local [*hukou* permits](/wiki/Hukou_system "Hukou system"), which entitles them to permanent residence in Beijing.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^ The remaining 8 million residents had *hukou* permits elsewhere and were not eligible to receive some social benefits provided by the Beijing municipal government.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^{#cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_158-6}

The population increased in 2013 by 455,000 or about 7% from the previous year and continued a decade-long trend of rapid growth.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^ The total population in 2004 was 14.213 million.^[\[164\]](#cite_note-2004pop-170)^ The population gains are driven largely by migration. The population's [rate of natural increase](/wiki/Rate_of_natural_increase "Rate of natural increase") in 2013 was a mere 0.441%, based on a [birth rate](/wiki/Birth_rate "Birth rate") of 8.93 and a [mortality rate](/wiki/Mortality_rate "Mortality rate") of 4.52.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^ The [gender balance](/wiki/Human_sex_ratio "Human sex ratio") was 51.6% males and 48.4% females.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-2013_Beijing_Stats-158)^{#cite_ref-2013_Beijing_Stats_158-9}

Working age people account for nearly 73.6% of the population.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^ Compared to 2004, residents age 0--14 as a proportion of the population dropped from 9.95% to 9.92% in 2013, but again increased to 12.1% in 2021.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^ Residents over the age of 65 declined from 11.12% to 8.58%, but increased to 14.2% in 2021.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^ From 2002 to 2011, the percentage of city residents with at least some college education nearly doubled, from 20.4% to 37.3%, and further increased to 49.1% by 2021.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^ About 66.4% have senior secondary school education and 88.2% had reached middle school.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-data2022-144)^{#cite_ref-data2022_144-9}

According to the 2010 census, nearly 96% of Beijing's population are ethnic [Han Chinese](/wiki/Han_Chinese "Han Chinese").^[\[165\]](#cite_note-2010census-171)^ Of the 800,000 ethnic minority population living in the capital, [Manchu](/wiki/Manchu_people "Manchu people") (336,000), [Hui](/wiki/Hui_people_in_Beijing "Hui people in Beijing") (249,000), [Korean](/wiki/Korean_people_in_Beijing "Korean people in Beijing") (77,000), [Mongol](/wiki/Mongol "Mongol") (37,000) and [Tujia](/wiki/Tujia_people "Tujia people") (24,000) constitute the five largest groups.^[\[166\]](#cite_note-2010minorities-172)^ In addition, there were 8,045 Hong Kong residents, 500 [Macau](/wiki/Macau "Macau") residents, and 7,772 Taiwan residents along with 91,128 registered foreigners living in Beijing.^[\[165\]](#cite_note-2010census-171)^ A study by the Beijing Academy of Sciences estimates that in 2010 there were on average 200,000 foreigners living in Beijing on any given day including students, business travellers and tourists that are not counted as registered residents.^[\[167\]](#cite_note-173)^{#cite_ref-173}

In 2017 the Chinese government implemented population controls for Beijing and Shanghai to fight what it called the "big city disease" which includes congestion, pollution, and shortages of education and health care services. From this policy, Beijing's population declined by 20,000 from 2016 to 2017.^[\[168\]](#cite_note-cap-174)^ Some low-income people are being forcibly removed from the city as both legal and illegal housing is being demolished in some high-density residential neighborhoods.^[\[168\]](#cite_note-cap-174)^ The population is being redistributed to [Jing-Jin-Ji](/wiki/Jing-Jin-Ji "Jing-Jin-Ji") and [Xiong'an New Area](/wiki/Xiong%27an_New_Area "Xiong'an New Area"), the transfer to the latter expected to include 300,000-500,000 people working in government research, universities, and corporate headquarters.^[\[169\]](#cite_note-175)^^[\[170\]](#cite_note-176)^{#cite_ref-176}  

Education and research {#Education_and_research}
------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Education and research")\]  
Main articles: [Education in Beijing](/wiki/Education_in_Beijing "Education in Beijing"), [Education in China](/wiki/Education_in_China "Education in China"), and [Higher education in China](/wiki/Higher_education_in_China "Higher education in China")  
See also: [Rankings of universities in China](/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_China "Rankings of universities in China"), [List of universities in China](/wiki/List_of_universities_in_China "List of universities in China"), and [Double First Class University Plan](/wiki/Double_First_Class_University_Plan "Double First Class University Plan")

Beijing is a world-leading center for scientific and technological innovation. It has been ranked the [No. 1](/wiki/List_of_cities_by_scientific_output "List of cities by scientific output") city in the world with the largest scientific research output, as tracked by the [Nature Index](/wiki/Nature_Index "Nature Index") since the list's inception in 2016.^[\[35\]](#cite_note-:10-38)^^[\[171\]](#cite_note-:7-177)^^[\[36\]](#cite_note-:9-39)^ The capital also leads the world with the highest share of articles published in the [natural sciences](/wiki/Natural_science "Natural science"), especially in the United Nations 17 [Sustainable Development Goals](/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals "Sustainable Development Goals") (SDGs)-related output.^[\[172\]](#cite_note-178)^^[\[173\]](#cite_note-179)^^[\[174\]](#cite_note-180)^^[\[175\]](#cite_note-181)^^[\[176\]](#cite_note-182)^ As of 2024, it stands as the most prolific scientific research center in [biological sciences](/wiki/Biological_sciences "Biological sciences") and [health science](/wiki/Health_science "Health science") in the Asia-Pacific, ranking third and sixth in the world, respectively.^[\[177\]](#cite_note-183)^^[\[178\]](#cite_note-184)^{#cite_ref-184}

Beijing has over [90 public colleges and universities](/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Beijing "List of universities and colleges in Beijing"), making it the largest urban [public university](/wiki/Public_university "Public university") system in Asia and the first city in China with the most higher education [institutions](/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Beijing "List of universities and colleges in Beijing").^[\[179\]](#cite_note-Beijing's_Universities-185)^^[\[180\]](#cite_note-:13-186)^ It is also home to the two best universities ([Tsinghua](/wiki/Tsinghua_University "Tsinghua University") and [Peking](/wiki/Peking_University "Peking University")) in the whole of the Asia \& Oceania region and emerging countries, with their rankings at #12 and #13 places in the world, respectively by the 2025 [Times Higher Education World University Rankings](/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings "Times Higher Education World University Rankings").^[\[32\]](#cite_note-:15-35)^^[\[181\]](#cite_note-:6-187)^^[\[33\]](#cite_note-:8-36)^ Both are members of the [C9 League](/wiki/C9_League "C9 League"), an alliance of elite Chinese universities offering comprehensive and leading education.^[\[182\]](#cite_note-188)^{#cite_ref-188}

Beijing also has the highest number of universities of any city in the country, representing more than one-fifth of [147 Double First-Class Universities](/wiki/Double_First_Class_University_Plan "Double First Class University Plan"), a national plan to develop elite Chinese universities into world-class institutions by the end of 2050.^[\[183\]](#cite_note-189)^ According to the [U.S. News \& World Report Best Global University Ranking](/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report_Best_Global_Universities_Ranking "U.S. News & World Report Best Global Universities Ranking") for 2024, Beijing has the highest number of universities among the major cities in the world included in the ranking, totaling 29.^[\[184\]](#cite_note-:522-190)^ A number of Beijing's [most prestigious universities](/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_China "Rankings of universities in China") consistently rank among the best in the [Asia-Pacific](/wiki/Asia-Pacific "Asia-Pacific") and the world, including [Peking University](/wiki/Peking_University "Peking University"), [Tsinghua University](/wiki/Tsinghua_University "Tsinghua University"), [Renmin University of China](/wiki/Renmin_University_of_China "Renmin University of China"), [Beijing Normal University](/wiki/Beijing_Normal_University "Beijing Normal University"), [University of Chinese Academy of Sciences](/wiki/University_of_the_Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences "University of the Chinese Academy of Sciences"), [Beihang University](/wiki/Beihang_University "Beihang University"), [Beijing Institute of Technology](/wiki/Beijing_Institute_of_Technology "Beijing Institute of Technology"), [China Agricultural University](/wiki/China_Agricultural_University "China Agricultural University"), [Minzu University of China](/wiki/Minzu_University_of_China "Minzu University of China"), [University of Science and Technology Beijing](/wiki/University_of_Science_and_Technology_Beijing "University of Science and Technology Beijing"), [Beijing University of Chemical Technology](/wiki/Beijing_University_of_Chemical_Technology "Beijing University of Chemical Technology"), [University of International Business and Economics](/wiki/University_of_International_Business_and_Economics_(Beijing) "University of International Business and Economics (Beijing)"), [University of Chinese Academy of Social Sciences](/wiki/University_of_Chinese_Academy_of_Social_Sciences "University of Chinese Academy of Social Sciences") and [Central University of Finance and Economics](/wiki/Central_University_of_Finance_and_Economics "Central University of Finance and Economics").^[\[185\]](#cite_note-:4-191)^^[\[29\]](#cite_note-:5-32)^^[\[186\]](#cite_note-:11-192)^^[\[187\]](#cite_note-193)^ These universities were selected as "[985 universities](/wiki/Project_985 "Project 985")" or "[211 universities](/wiki/Project_211 "Project 211")" by the Chinese government in order to build world-class universities.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-194)^^[\[189\]](#cite_note-195)^{#cite_ref-195}

The city is a seat of the [Chinese Academy of Sciences](/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences "Chinese Academy of Sciences"), which has been consistently ranked the No. 1 research institute in the world by *[Nature Index](/wiki/Nature_Index "Nature Index")* since the list's inception in 2014.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-196)^^[\[191\]](#cite_note-197)^^[\[192\]](#cite_note-198)^ The academy also runs the [University of the Chinese Academy of Sciences](/wiki/University_of_the_Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences "University of the Chinese Academy of Sciences"), which is located in Beijing and ranked among the world's top five research institutions by the [Nature Index](/wiki/Nature_Index "Nature Index").^[\[193\]](#cite_note-199)^ Beijing is also a site of the [Chinese Academy of Engineering](/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Engineering "Chinese Academy of Engineering"), the [China Academy of Space Technology](/wiki/China_Academy_of_Space_Technology "China Academy of Space Technology"), the [China Academy of Engineering Physics](/wiki/China_Academy_of_Engineering_Physics "China Academy of Engineering Physics"), the [Chinese Academy of Social Sciences](/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Social_Sciences "Chinese Academy of Social Sciences"), the [Chinese Academy of Agricultural Sciences](/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Agricultural_Sciences "Chinese Academy of Agricultural Sciences"), the [Chinese Academy of Cultural Heritage](/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Cultural_Heritage "Chinese Academy of Cultural Heritage"), the [Chinese Academy of Geological Sciences](/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Geological_Sciences "Chinese Academy of Geological Sciences"), the [Chinese Academy of Fishery Sciences](/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Fishery_Sciences "Chinese Academy of Fishery Sciences"), the [China Academy of Chinese Medical Sciences](/w/index.php?title=China_Academy_of_Chinese_Medical_Sciences&action=edit&redlink=1 "China Academy of Chinese Medical Sciences (page does not exist)") and the [National Natural Science Foundation of China](/wiki/National_Natural_Science_Foundation_of_China "National Natural Science Foundation of China").{#cite_ref-199}

Some of the [national key universities](/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Beijing "List of universities and colleges in Beijing") in Beijing are:  
* [Beijing Forestry University](/wiki/Beijing_Forestry_University "Beijing Forestry University")
* [Beijing Jiaotong University](/wiki/Beijing_Jiaotong_University "Beijing Jiaotong University")
* [Beijing University of Technology](/wiki/Beijing_University_of_Technology "Beijing University of Technology")
* [Beijing University of Chinese Medicine](/wiki/Beijing_University_of_Chinese_Medicine "Beijing University of Chinese Medicine")
* [Beijing University of Posts and Telecommunications](/wiki/Beijing_University_of_Posts_and_Telecommunications "Beijing University of Posts and Telecommunications")
* [Beijing Electronic Science and Technology Institute](/wiki/Beijing_Electronic_Science_and_Technology_Institute "Beijing Electronic Science and Technology Institute")
* [Beijing Foreign Studies University](/wiki/Beijing_Foreign_Studies_University "Beijing Foreign Studies University")
* [Beijing Language and Culture University](/wiki/Beijing_Language_and_Culture_University "Beijing Language and Culture University")
* [Beijing Sport University](/wiki/Beijing_Sport_University "Beijing Sport University")
* [Central Conservatory of Music](/wiki/Central_Conservatory_of_Music "Central Conservatory of Music")
* [Central Academy of Fine Arts](/wiki/Central_Academy_of_Fine_Arts "Central Academy of Fine Arts")
* [Central Academy of Drama](/wiki/Central_Academy_of_Drama "Central Academy of Drama")
* [China University of Geosciences (Beijing)](/wiki/China_University_of_Geosciences_(Beijing) "China University of Geosciences (Beijing)")
* [China University of Petroleum (Beijing)](/wiki/China_University_of_Petroleum_(Beijing) "China University of Petroleum (Beijing)")
* [China University of Mining and Technology (Beijing)](/wiki/China_University_of_Mining_and_Technology_(Beijing) "China University of Mining and Technology (Beijing)")
* [China University of Political Science and Law](/wiki/China_University_of_Political_Science_and_Law "China University of Political Science and Law")
* [China Foreign Affairs University](/wiki/China_Foreign_Affairs_University "China Foreign Affairs University")
* [Chinese People's Public Security University](/wiki/Chinese_People%27s_Public_Security_University "Chinese People's Public Security University")
* [China Women's University](/wiki/China_Women%27s_University "China Women's University")
* [China Youth University for Political Sciences](/wiki/China_Youth_University_for_Political_Sciences "China Youth University for Political Sciences")
* [China Institute of Industrial Relations](/wiki/China_Institute_of_Industrial_Relations "China Institute of Industrial Relations")
* [Communication University of China](/wiki/Communication_University_of_China "Communication University of China")
* [North China Electric Power University](/wiki/North_China_Electric_Power_University "North China Electric Power University")
* [Peking Union Medical College](/wiki/Peking_Union_Medical_College "Peking Union Medical College")
* [University of International Relations](/wiki/University_of_International_Relations "University of International Relations")

Beijing is also home to several religious institutions, Some of them are listed as follows:  
* [China Islamic Institute](/w/index.php?title=China_Islamic_Institute&action=edit&redlink=1 "China Islamic Institute (page does not exist)") \[[zh](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9B%BD%E4%BC%8A%E6%96%AF%E5%85%B0%E6%95%99%E7%BB%8F%E5%AD%A6%E9%99%A2 "zh:中国伊斯兰教经学院")\] (中国伊斯兰教经学院)
* [Beijing Islamic Institute](/w/index.php?title=Beijing_Islamic_Institute&action=edit&redlink=1 "Beijing Islamic Institute (page does not exist)") \[[zh](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%8C%97%E4%BA%AC%E4%BC%8A%E6%96%AF%E5%85%B0%E6%95%99%E7%BB%8F%E5%AD%A6%E9%99%A2 "zh:北京伊斯兰教经学院")\] (北京伊斯兰教经学院)
* [The Buddhist Academy of China](/w/index.php?title=The_Buddhist_Academy_of_China&action=edit&redlink=1 "The Buddhist Academy of China (page does not exist)") \[[zh](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9B%BD%E4%BD%9B%E5%AD%A6%E9%99%A2 "zh:中国佛学院")\] (中国佛学院)
* [High-level Tibetan Buddhism College of China](/w/index.php?title=High-level_Tibetan_Buddhism_College_of_China&action=edit&redlink=1 "High-level Tibetan Buddhism College of China (page does not exist)") \[[zh](https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9B%BD%E8%97%8F%E8%AF%AD%E7%B3%BB%E9%AB%98%E7%BA%A7%E4%BD%9B%E5%AD%A6%E9%99%A2 "zh:中国藏语系高级佛学院")\] (中国藏语系高级佛学院)
* [National Seminary of Catholic Church in China](/wiki/National_Seminary_of_Catholic_Church_in_China "National Seminary of Catholic Church in China") (中国天主教神哲学院)

The city's [compulsory education](/wiki/Compulsory_education "Compulsory education") system is among the best in the world: in 2018, 15-year-old students from Beijing (together with [Shanghai](/wiki/Shanghai "Shanghai"), [Zhejiang](/wiki/Zhejiang "Zhejiang") and [Jiangsu](/wiki/Jiangsu "Jiangsu")) outperformed all of the other 78 participating countries in all categories (math, reading, and science) in the [Program for International Student Assessment](/wiki/Program_for_International_Student_Assessment "Program for International Student Assessment"), a worldwide study of academic performance conducted by the OECD.^[\[194\]](#cite_note-PISA2018-200)^{#cite_ref-PISA2018_200-0}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Culture")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ancient_Beijing_observatory_10.jpg/220px-Ancient_Beijing_observatory_10.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ancient_Beijing_observatory_10.jpg) The [Beijing Ancient Observatory](/wiki/Beijing_Ancient_Observatory "Beijing Ancient Observatory")

People native to urban Beijing speak the [Beijing dialect](/wiki/Beijing_dialect "Beijing dialect"), which belongs to the Mandarin subdivision of [spoken Chinese](/wiki/Chinese_spoken_language "Chinese spoken language"). This speech is the basis for *[putonghua](/wiki/Putonghua "Putonghua")* , the standard spoken language used in mainland China and [Taiwan](/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan"), and one of the four official languages of [Singapore](/wiki/Singapore "Singapore"). Rural areas of Beijing Municipality have [their own dialects](/wiki/Jilu_Mandarin "Jilu Mandarin") akin to those of Hebei province, which surrounds Beijing Municipality.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Beijing or [Peking opera](/wiki/Peking_opera "Peking opera") is a traditional form of Chinese theater well known throughout the nation. Commonly lauded as one of the highest achievements of [Chinese culture](/wiki/Chinese_culture "Chinese culture"), Beijing opera is performed through a combination of song, spoken dialogue, and codified action sequences involving gestures, movement, fighting and acrobatics. Much of Beijing opera is carried out in an archaic stage dialect quite different from Modern Standard Chinese and from the modern Beijing dialect.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-201)^{#cite_ref-201}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Sliced_Peking_Duck.jpg/220px-Sliced_Peking_Duck.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sliced_Peking_Duck.jpg) Sliced [Peking duck](/wiki/Peking_duck "Peking duck") served with traditional condiments

[Beijing cuisine](/wiki/Beijing_cuisine "Beijing cuisine") is the local style of cooking. [Peking duck](/wiki/Peking_duck "Peking duck") is perhaps the best known dish. [Fuling jiabing](/wiki/Fuling_jiabing "Fuling jiabing"), a traditional Beijing snack food, is a pancake (*bing* ) resembling a flat disk with a filling made from *[fu ling](/wiki/Fu_Ling "Fu Ling")* , a fungus used in traditional [Chinese medicine](/wiki/Chinese_medicine "Chinese medicine"). [Teahouses](/wiki/Teahouse "Teahouse") are also common in Beijing.

The [cloisonné](/wiki/Cloisonn%C3%A9 "Cloisonné") (or *Jingtailan* , literally "Blue of [Jingtai](/wiki/Jingtai_Emperor "Jingtai Emperor")") metalworking technique and tradition is a Beijing art speciality, and is one of the most revered traditional crafts in China. Cloisonné making requires elaborate and complicated processes which include base-hammering, copper-strip inlay, soldering, enamel-filling, enamel-firing, surface polishing and gilding.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-202)^ Beijing's [lacquerware](/wiki/Lacquerware "Lacquerware") is also well known for its sophisticated and intricate patterns and images carved into its surface, and the various decoration techniques of lacquer include "carved lacquer" and "engraved gold".{#cite_ref-202}

Younger residents of Beijing have become more attracted to the nightlife, which has flourished in recent decades, breaking prior cultural traditions that had practically restricted it to the upper class.^[\[197\]](#cite_note-203)^ Today, [Houhai](/wiki/Houhai "Houhai"), [Sanlitun](/wiki/Sanlitun "Sanlitun") and [Wudaokou](/wiki/Wudaokou "Wudaokou") are Beijing's nightlife hotspots.{#cite_ref-203}

In 2012 Beijing was named as City of Design and became part of the [UNESCO Creative Cities Network](/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network "Creative Cities Network").^[\[198\]](#cite_note-204)^{#cite_ref-204}  

### Places of interest {#Places_of_interest}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Places of interest")\]  
See also: [Major National Historical and Cultural Sites (Beijing)](/wiki/Major_National_Historical_and_Cultural_Sites_(Beijing) "Major National Historical and Cultural Sites (Beijing)") and [List of Beijing landmarks](/wiki/List_of_Beijing_landmarks "List of Beijing landmarks")
> ...the city remains an epicenter of tradition with the treasures of nearly 2,000 years as the imperial capital still on view---in the famed Forbidden City and in the city's lush pavilions and gardens...  
> --- [National Geographic](/wiki/National_Geographic_Society "National Geographic Society")^[\[199\]](#cite_note-national-205)^
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/20130830-BJ-Zhengyangmen%28Qianmen%29_%E6%AD%A3%E9%98%B3%E9%97%A8%E7%AE%AD%E6%A5%BC_2.JPG/220px-20130830-BJ-Zhengyangmen%28Qianmen%29_%E6%AD%A3%E9%98%B3%E9%97%A8%E7%AE%AD%E6%A5%BC_2.JPG)](/wiki/File:20130830-BJ-Zhengyangmen(Qianmen)_%E6%AD%A3%E9%98%B3%E9%97%A8%E7%AE%AD%E6%A5%BC_2.JPG) [Qianmen Avenue](/wiki/Qianmen_Avenue "Qianmen Avenue") is a traditional commercial street outside Qianmen Gate along the southern Central Axis.

At the historical heart of Beijing lies the [Forbidden City](/wiki/Forbidden_City "Forbidden City"), the enormous palace compound that was the home of the emperors of the [Ming](/wiki/Ming_dynasty "Ming dynasty") and [Qing](/wiki/Qing_dynasty "Qing dynasty") dynasties;^[\[200\]](#cite_note-206)^ the Forbidden City hosts the Palace Museum, which contains imperial collections of Chinese art. Surrounding the Forbidden City are several former imperial gardens, parks and scenic areas, notably [Beihai](/wiki/Beihai_Park "Beihai Park"), [Shichahai](/wiki/Shichahai "Shichahai"), [Zhongnanhai](/wiki/Zhongnanhai "Zhongnanhai"), [Jingshan](/wiki/Jingshan_Park "Jingshan Park") and [Zhongshan](/wiki/Zhongshan_Park_(Beijing) "Zhongshan Park (Beijing)"). These places, particularly Beihai Park, are described as masterpieces of [Chinese gardening](/wiki/Chinese_garden "Chinese garden") art,^[\[201\]](#cite_note-207)^ and are tourist destinations of historical importance;^[\[202\]](#cite_note-208)^ in the modern era, Zhongnanhai has also been the political heart of various Chinese governments and regimes and is now the headquarters of the Chinese Communist Party and the State Council. From Tiananmen Square, right across from the Forbidden City, there are several notable sites, such as the Tiananmen, [Qianmen](/wiki/Qianmen "Qianmen"), the [Great Hall of the People](/wiki/Great_Hall_of_the_People "Great Hall of the People"), the [National Museum of China](/wiki/National_Museum_of_China "National Museum of China"), the [Monument to the People's Heroes](/wiki/Monument_to_the_People%27s_Heroes "Monument to the People's Heroes"), and the [Mausoleum of Mao Zedong](/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Mao_Zedong "Mausoleum of Mao Zedong"). The [Summer Palace](/wiki/Summer_Palace "Summer Palace") and the [Old Summer Palace](/wiki/Old_Summer_Palace "Old Summer Palace") both lie at the western part of the city; the former, a [UNESCO World Heritage Site](/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site "UNESCO World Heritage Site"),^[\[203\]](#cite_note-209)^ contains a comprehensive collection of imperial gardens and palaces that served as the summer retreats for the Qing imperial family.{#cite_ref-209}

Among the best known religious sites in the city is the [Temple of Heaven](/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven "Temple of Heaven") (*Tiantan* ), located in southeastern Beijing, also a UNESCO World Heritage Site,^[\[204\]](#cite_note-210)^ where emperors of the Ming and Qing dynasties made visits for annual ceremonies of prayers to Heaven for good harvest. In the north of the city is the [Temple of Earth](/wiki/Temple_of_Earth "Temple of Earth") (*Ditan* ), while the [Temple of the Sun](/wiki/Temple_of_the_Sun "Temple of the Sun") (*Ritan* ) and the [Temple of the Moon](/wiki/Temple_of_the_Moon_(China) "Temple of the Moon (China)") (*Yuetan* ) lie in the eastern and western urban areas respectively. Other well-known temple sites include the [Dongyue Temple](/wiki/Beijing_Dongyue_Temple "Beijing Dongyue Temple"), [Tanzhe Temple](/wiki/Tanzhe_Temple "Tanzhe Temple"), [Miaoying Temple](/wiki/Miaoying_Temple "Miaoying Temple"), [White Cloud Temple](/wiki/White_Cloud_Temple "White Cloud Temple"), [Yonghe Temple](/wiki/Yonghe_Temple "Yonghe Temple"), [Fayuan Temple](/wiki/Fayuan_Temple "Fayuan Temple"), [Wanshou Temple](/wiki/Wanshou_Temple "Wanshou Temple") and [Big Bell Temple](/wiki/Big_Bell_Temple "Big Bell Temple"). The city also has its own [Confucius Temple](/wiki/Beijing_Temple_of_Confucius "Beijing Temple of Confucius"), and a [Guozijian](/wiki/Guozijian_(Beijing) "Guozijian (Beijing)") or Imperial Academy. The [Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception](/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Immaculate_Conception_in_Beijing "Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception in Beijing"), built in 1605, is the oldest Catholic church in Beijing. The [Niujie Mosque](/wiki/Niujie_Mosque "Niujie Mosque") is the oldest mosque in Beijing, with a history stretching back over a thousand years.{#cite_ref-210}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Entrance_of_Universal_Studios_Beijing_%2820210907121707%29.jpg/220px-Entrance_of_Universal_Studios_Beijing_%2820210907121707%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Entrance_of_Universal_Studios_Beijing_(20210907121707).jpg) [Universal Studios Beijing](/wiki/Universal_Studios_Beijing "Universal Studios Beijing") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Happy_Valley_Beijing_%285%29.jpg/220px-Happy_Valley_Beijing_%285%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Happy_Valley_Beijing_(5).jpg) [Happy Valley Beijing](/wiki/Happy_Valley_Beijing "Happy Valley Beijing")

Beijing contains several well-preserved pagodas and stone pagodas, such as the towering [Pagoda of Tianning Temple](/wiki/Pagoda_of_Tianning_Temple_(Beijing) "Pagoda of Tianning Temple (Beijing)"), which was built during the Liao dynasty from 1100 to 1120, and the [Pagoda of Cishou Temple](/wiki/Pagoda_of_Cishou_Temple "Pagoda of Cishou Temple"), which was built in 1576 during the Ming dynasty. Historically noteworthy stone bridges include the 12th-century [Lugou Bridge](/wiki/Lugou_Bridge "Lugou Bridge"), the 17th-century [Baliqiao](/wiki/Baliqiao "Baliqiao") bridge, and the 18th-century [Jade Belt Bridge](/wiki/Jade_Belt_Bridge "Jade Belt Bridge"). The [Beijing Ancient Observatory](/wiki/Beijing_Ancient_Observatory "Beijing Ancient Observatory") displays pre-telescopic spheres dating back to the Ming and Qing dynasties. The [Fragrant Hills](/wiki/Fragrant_Hills "Fragrant Hills") (*Xiangshan* ) is a public park that consists of natural landscaped areas as well as traditional and cultural relics. The [Beijing Botanical Garden](/wiki/Beijing_Botanical_Garden "Beijing Botanical Garden") exhibits over 6,000 species of plants, including a variety of trees, bushes and flowers, and an extensive [peony](/wiki/Peony "Peony") garden. The [Taoranting](/wiki/Taoranting_Park "Taoranting Park"), [Longtan](/wiki/Longtan_Park "Longtan Park"), [Chaoyang](/wiki/Beijing_Chaoyang_Park "Beijing Chaoyang Park"), [Haidian](/wiki/Haidian_Park "Haidian Park"), [Milu Yuan](/wiki/Milu_Yuan "Milu Yuan") and [Zizhu Yuan](/wiki/Purple_Bamboo_Park "Purple Bamboo Park") parks are some of the notable recreational parks in the city. The [Beijing Zoo](/wiki/Beijing_Zoo "Beijing Zoo") is a center of zoological research that also contains rare animals from various continents, including the Chinese [giant panda](/wiki/Giant_panda "Giant panda").

There are 144 museums and galleries (as of June 2008^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit)^) in the city.^[\[205\]](#cite_note-211)^^[\[206\]](#cite_note-212)^^[\[207\]](#cite_note-museum-213)^ In addition to the Palace Museum in the Forbidden City and the National Museum of China, other major museums include the [National Art Museum of China](/wiki/National_Art_Museum_of_China "National Art Museum of China"), the [Capital Museum](/wiki/Capital_Museum "Capital Museum"), the [Beijing Art Museum](/wiki/Wanshou_Temple "Wanshou Temple"), the [Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution](/wiki/Military_Museum_of_the_Chinese_People%27s_Revolution "Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution"), the [Geological Museum of China](/wiki/Geological_Museum_of_China "Geological Museum of China"), the [Beijing Museum of Natural History](/wiki/Beijing_Museum_of_Natural_History "Beijing Museum of Natural History") and the [Paleozoological Museum of China](/wiki/Paleozoological_Museum_of_China "Paleozoological Museum of China").^[\[207\]](#cite_note-museum-213)^{#cite_ref-museum_213-1}

Located at the outskirts of urban Beijing, but within its municipality are the [Thirteen Tombs of the Ming dynasty](/wiki/Ming_tombs "Ming tombs"), the lavish and elaborate burial sites of thirteen Ming emperors, which have been designated as part of the UNESCO World Heritage Site [Imperial Tombs of the Ming and Qing Dynasties](/wiki/Imperial_Tombs_of_the_Ming_and_Qing_Dynasties "Imperial Tombs of the Ming and Qing Dynasties").^[\[208\]](#cite_note-214)^ The archaeological [Peking Man](/wiki/Peking_Man "Peking Man") site at [Zhoukoudian](/wiki/Zhoukoudian "Zhoukoudian") is another World Heritage Site within the municipality,^[\[209\]](#cite_note-215)^ containing a wealth of discoveries, among them one of the first specimens of *[Homo erectus](/wiki/Homo_erectus "Homo erectus")* and an assemblage of bones of the gigantic [hyena](/wiki/Hyena "Hyena") *[Pachycrocuta](/wiki/Pachycrocuta "Pachycrocuta") brevirostris* . There are several sections of the UNESCO World Heritage Site [Great Wall of China](/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China "Great Wall of China"),^[\[210\]](#cite_note-216)^ most notably [Badaling](/wiki/Badaling "Badaling"), [Jinshanling](/wiki/Jinshanling "Jinshanling"), [Simatai](/wiki/Simatai "Simatai") and [Mutianyu](/wiki/Mutianyu "Mutianyu"). According to the [World Travel \& Tourism Council](/wiki/World_Travel_and_Tourism_Council "World Travel and Tourism Council") (WTTC), Beijing is the second highest earning tourist city in the world after [Shanghai](/wiki/Shanghai "Shanghai").^[\[211\]](#cite_note-217)^ Theme parks located within the city include [Universal Studios Beijing](/wiki/Universal_Studios_Beijing "Universal Studios Beijing") and [Happy Valley Beijing](/wiki/Happy_Valley_Beijing "Happy Valley Beijing"), both of which are among the most visited theme parks in Asia.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-218)^{#cite_ref-218}  

### Intangible cultural heritage {#Intangible_cultural_heritage}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Intangible cultural heritage")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Beijing-Opera2.jpg/170px-Beijing-Opera2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Beijing-Opera2.jpg) [Peking opera](/wiki/Peking_opera "Peking opera")

The cultural heritage of Beijing is rich and diverse. Starting 2006, the Beijing government started the process of selecting and preserving cultural heritages. Five cultural heritage lists have been published over the years. 288 distinct practices are categorized as cultural heritage. These 288 cultural heritages are further divided into ten categories, namely folk music, folk dance, traditional opera, melodious art, juggling and game, folk art, traditional handicraft, traditional medicine, folk literature and folklore.^[\[213\]](#cite_note-219)^^[\[214\]](#cite_note-220)^^[\[215\]](#cite_note-221)^^[\[216\]](#cite_note-222)^{#cite_ref-222}  
* Folk music
  * [Zhihua Temple](/wiki/Zhihua_Temple "Zhihua Temple") music
  * Tongzhou [shanty](/wiki/Sea_shanty "Sea shanty")
* Folk dance
  * Tongzhou [Dragon dance](/wiki/Dragon_dance "Dragon dance")
  * Miliangtun [Stilts](/wiki/Stilts "Stilts")
* Traditional opera
  * [Kunqu](/wiki/Kunqu "Kunqu")
  * [Peking opera](/wiki/Peking_opera "Peking opera")
* Melodious art
  * [Xiangsheng](/wiki/Xiangsheng "Xiangsheng")
* Acrobatic Performance and game
  * [Weiqi(Go)](/wiki/Go_(game) "Go (game)")
  * [Xiangqi](/wiki/Xiangqi "Xiangqi")
* Folk art
  * [Ivory carving](/wiki/Ivory_carving "Ivory carving")
* Traditional handicraft
  * [Peking duck](/wiki/Peking_duck "Peking duck") manufacturing techniques
  * [Cloisonné](/wiki/Cloisonn%C3%A9 "Cloisonné") manufacturing techniques
* Traditional medicine
  * [Tong Ren Tang](/wiki/Tong_Ren_Tang "Tong Ren Tang") culture
* Folk literature
* Folklore
  * [Miaohui](/wiki/Miaohui "Miaohui")
* [Lantern Festival](/wiki/Lantern_Festival "Lantern Festival")  

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Religion")\]

The religious heritage of Beijing is rich and diverse as [Chinese folk religion](/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion "Chinese folk religion"), [Taoism](/wiki/Taoism "Taoism"), [Buddhism](/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"), [Confucianism](/wiki/Confucianism "Confucianism"), [Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam") and [Christianity](/wiki/Christianity "Christianity") all have significant historical presence in the city. As the national capital, the city also hosts the [State Administration for Religious Affairs](/wiki/State_Administration_for_Religious_Affairs "State Administration for Religious Affairs") and various state-sponsored institutions of the leading religions.^[\[217\]](#cite_note-religion1-223)^ In recent decades, foreign residents have brought other religions to the city.^[\[217\]](#cite_note-religion1-223)^ According to Wang Zhiyun of the Chinese Academy of Social Sciences in 2010 there were 2.2 million Buddhists in the city, equal to 11.2% of the total population.^[\[218\]](#cite_note-224)^ According to the Chinese General Social Survey of 2009, Christians constitute 0.78% of the city's population.^[\[219\]](#cite_note-Wang2015-225)^ According to a 2010 survey, Muslims constitute 1.76% of the population of Beijing.^[\[220\]](#cite_note-2010-Islam-226)^{#cite_ref-2010-Islam_226-0}  

### Chinese folk religion and Taoism {#Chinese_folk_religion_and_Taoism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Chinese folk religion and Taoism")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Di%27anmen_Fire_God_Temple%2C_Beijing_5.jpg/220px-Di%27anmen_Fire_God_Temple%2C_Beijing_5.jpg)](/wiki/File:Di%27anmen_Fire_God_Temple,_Beijing_5.jpg) Fire God Temple in Di'anmen

Beijing has many temples dedicated to [folk religious and communal deities](/wiki/Chinese_gods_and_immortals "Chinese gods and immortals"), many of which are being reconstructed or refurbished in the 2000s and 2010s. Yearly sacrifices to the [God of Heaven](/wiki/Tian "Tian") ([祭天](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%A5%AD%E5%A4%A9 "wikt:祭天"); *jìtiān* ) at the [Temple of Heaven](/wiki/Temple_of_Heaven "Temple of Heaven") have been resumed by [Confucian](/wiki/Confucianism "Confucianism") groups in the 2010s.

There are temples dedicated to the worship of the Goddess ([娘娘](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%A8%98%E5%A8%98 "wikt:娘娘"); *Niángniáng* ) in the city, one of them near the [Olympic Village](/wiki/Beijing_Olympic_Village "Beijing Olympic Village"), and they revolve around a major cult center at [Mount Miaofeng](/wiki/Mount_Miaofeng "Mount Miaofeng"). There are also many temples consecrated to the [Dragon God](/wiki/Dragon_King "Dragon King"), to the Medicine Master ([药](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%8D%AF "wikt:药")[王](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%8E%8B "wikt:王"); *Yàowáng* ), to [Divus Guan (Guan Yu)](/wiki/Guan_Yu "Guan Yu"), to the Fire God ([火神](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%81%AB%E7%A5%9E "wikt:火神"); *Huǒshén* ), to the [Wealth God](/wiki/Caishen "Caishen"), temples of the [City God](/wiki/Chenghuangshen "Chenghuangshen"), and at least one temple consecrated to the [Yellow Deity](/wiki/Yellow_Emperor "Yellow Emperor") of the [Chariot](/wiki/Big_Dipper "Big Dipper") [Shaft](/wiki/Axis_mundi "Axis mundi") ([轩辕](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%BD%A9%E8%BE%95 "wikt:轩辕")[黄帝](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%BB%84%E5%B8%9D "wikt:黄帝"); *Xuānyuán Huángdì* ) in [Pinggu District](/wiki/Pinggu_District "Pinggu District"). Many of these temples are governed by the Beijing Taoist Association, such as the [Fire God Temple of the Shicha Lake](/wiki/Huode_Zhenjun_Temple "Huode Zhenjun Temple"), while many others are not and are governed by popular committees and locals. A great Temple of Xuanyuan Huangdi will be built in Pinggu (possibly as an expansion of the already existing shrine) within 2020, and the temple will feature a statue of the deity which will be amongst the [tallest in the world](/wiki/List_of_tallest_statues "List of tallest statues").^[\[221\]](#cite_note-227)^^[\[222\]](#cite_note-228)^{#cite_ref-228}

The national [Chinese Taoist Association](/wiki/Chinese_Taoist_Association "Chinese Taoist Association") and Chinese Taoist College have their headquarters at the [White Cloud Temple](/wiki/White_Cloud_Temple "White Cloud Temple") of [Quanzhen Taoism](/wiki/Quanzhen_Taoism "Quanzhen Taoism"), which was founded in 741 and rebuilt numerous times. The [Beijing Dongyue Temple](/wiki/Beijing_Dongyue_Temple "Beijing Dongyue Temple") outside Chaoyangmen is the largest temple of [Zhengyi Taoism](/wiki/Zhengyi_Taoism "Zhengyi Taoism") in the city. The local Beijing Taoist Association has its headquarters at the [Lüzu Temple](/wiki/L%C3%BCzu_Temple "Lüzu Temple") near Fuxingmen.^[\[223\]](#cite_note-229)^{#cite_ref-229}  

### Buddhism {#Buddhism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Buddhism")\]
