[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/%E5%8D%81%E6%96%B9%E6%99%AE%E5%90%8C%E5%A1%94%28%E5%83%A7%E4%BA%BA%E5%90%88%E8%91%AC%E5%A1%94%29_-_Pagoda_for_Ordinary_Monks_-_2012.04_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-%E5%8D%81%E6%96%B9%E6%99%AE%E5%90%8C%E5%A1%94%28%E5%83%A7%E4%BA%BA%E5%90%88%E8%91%AC%E5%A1%94%29_-_Pagoda_for_Ordinary_Monks_-_2012.04_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:%E5%8D%81%E6%96%B9%E6%99%AE%E5%90%8C%E5%A1%94(%E5%83%A7%E4%BA%BA%E5%90%88%E8%91%AC%E5%A1%94)_-_Pagoda_for_Ordinary_Monks_-_2012.04_-_panoramio.jpg) The tomb pagodas at [Tanzhe Temple](/wiki/Tanzhe_Temple "Tanzhe Temple") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Dongcheng%2C_Beijing%2C_China_-_panoramio_%2884%29.jpg/220px-Dongcheng%2C_Beijing%2C_China_-_panoramio_%2884%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Dongcheng,_Beijing,_China_-_panoramio_(84).jpg) [Yonghe Temple](/wiki/Yonghe_Temple "Yonghe Temple") of [Tibetan Buddhism](/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism "Tibetan Buddhism")

11% of the population of Beijing practices [East Asian Buddhism](/wiki/East_Asian_Buddhism "East Asian Buddhism")^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^. The [Buddhist Association of China](/wiki/Buddhist_Association_of_China "Buddhist Association of China"), the state's supervisory organ overseeing all [Buddhist](/wiki/Buddhist "Buddhist") institutions in mainland China, is headquartered in the [Guangji Temple](/wiki/Guangji_Temple_(Beijing) "Guangji Temple (Beijing)"), a temple founded over 800 years ago during the [Jin dynasty (1115--1234)](/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234) "Jin dynasty (1115–1234)") in what is now [Fuchengmennei](/wiki/Fuchengmen "Fuchengmen") (阜成门内). The Beijing Buddhist Association along with the Buddhist Choir and Orchestra are based in the [Guanghua Temple](/wiki/Guanghua_Temple_(Beijing) "Guanghua Temple (Beijing)"), which dates to the Yuan dynasty over 700 years ago. The Buddhist Academy of China and its library are housed in the [Fayuan Temple](/wiki/Fayuan_Temple "Fayuan Temple") near [Caishikou](/wiki/Caishikou "Caishikou"). The Fayuan Temple, which dates to the [Tang dynasty](/wiki/Tang_dynasty "Tang dynasty") 1300 years ago, is the oldest temple in urban Beijing. The [Tongjiao Temple](/wiki/Tongjiao_Temple "Tongjiao Temple") inside [Dongzhimen](/wiki/Dongzhimen "Dongzhimen") is the city's only Buddhist nunnery.

The [Xihuang Temple](/wiki/Xihuang_Temple "Xihuang Temple") originally dates to the [Liao dynasty](/wiki/Liao_dynasty "Liao dynasty"). In 1651, the temple was commissioned by the [Qing Emperor Shunzhi](/wiki/Shunzhi_Emperor "Shunzhi Emperor") to host the visit of the [Fifth Dalai Lama](/wiki/5th_Dalai_Lama "5th Dalai Lama") to Beijing. Since then, this temple has hosted the [13th Dalai Lama](/wiki/13th_Dalai_Lama "13th Dalai Lama") as well as the [Sixth](/wiki/Lobsang_Palden_Yeshe,_6th_Panchen_Lama "Lobsang Palden Yeshe, 6th Panchen Lama"), [Ninth](/wiki/Thubten_Choekyi_Nyima,_9th_Panchen_Lama "Thubten Choekyi Nyima, 9th Panchen Lama") and [Tenth](/wiki/Choekyi_Gyaltsen,_10th_Panchen_Lama "Choekyi Gyaltsen, 10th Panchen Lama") Panchen Lamas.

The largest Tibetan Buddhist Temple in Beijing is the [Yonghe Temple](/wiki/Yonghe_Temple "Yonghe Temple"), which was decreed by the [Qing Emperor Qianlong](/wiki/Qianlong_Emperor "Qianlong Emperor") in 1744 to serve as the residence and research facility for his Buddhist preceptor of [Rölpé Dorjé](/wiki/Changkya_R%C3%B6lp%C3%A9_Dorj%C3%A9 "Changkya Rölpé Dorjé") the third [Changkya](/wiki/Changkya_Khutukhtu "Changkya Khutukhtu") (or living Buddha of [Inner Mongolia](/wiki/Inner_Mongolia "Inner Mongolia")). The Yonghe Temple is so-named because it was the childhood residence of the [Yongzheng Emperor](/wiki/Yongzheng_Emperor "Yongzheng Emperor"), and retains the [glazed tiles](/wiki/Chinese_glazed_roof_tile "Chinese glazed roof tile") reserved for imperial palaces. While the "High-level Tibetan Buddhism College of China", China's highest institution college of Tibetan Buddhism, situated near the Yonghe Temple. The [Lingguang Temple](/wiki/Lingguang_Temple_(Beijing) "Lingguang Temple (Beijing)") of [Badachu](/wiki/Badachu "Badachu") in the [Western Hills](/wiki/Western_Hills "Western Hills") also dates to the Tang dynasty. The temple's Zhaoxian Pagoda (招仙塔) was first built in 1071 during the Liao dynasty to hold a tooth relic of the [Buddha](/wiki/Gautama_Buddha "Gautama Buddha"). The pagoda was destroyed during the [Boxer Rebellion](/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion "Boxer Rebellion") and the tooth was discovered from its foundation. A new pagoda was built in 1964. The six aforementioned temples: Guangji, Guanghua, Tongjiao, Xihuang, Yonghe and Lingguang have been designated [National Key Buddhist Temples in Han Chinese Area](/wiki/National_Key_Buddhist_Temples_in_Han_Chinese_Area "National Key Buddhist Temples in Han Chinese Area").

In addition, other notable temples in Beijing include the [Tanzhe Temple](/wiki/Tanzhe_Temple "Tanzhe Temple") (founded in the [Jin dynasty (266--420)](/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(266%E2%80%93420) "Jin dynasty (266–420)") is the oldest in the municipality), the [Tianning Temple](/wiki/Tianning_Temple_(Beijing) "Tianning Temple (Beijing)") (oldest pagoda in the city), the [Miaoying Temple](/wiki/Miaoying_Temple "Miaoying Temple") (famed for [Yuan](/wiki/Yuan_dynasty "Yuan dynasty")-era white pagoda), the [Wanshou Temple](/wiki/Wanshou_Temple "Wanshou Temple") (home to the [Beijing Art Museum](/wiki/Beijing_Art_Museum "Beijing Art Museum")) and the [Big Bell Temple](/wiki/Big_Bell_Temple "Big Bell Temple") (Dazhong Temple).  

### Islam {#Islam}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Islam")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Niujie_Mosques02.jpg/220px-Niujie_Mosques02.jpg)](/wiki/File:Niujie_Mosques02.jpg) [Niujie Mosque](/wiki/Niujie_Mosque "Niujie Mosque")

Beijing has about 70 mosques recognized by the [Islamic Association of China](/wiki/Islamic_Association_of_China "Islamic Association of China"), whose headquarters are located next to the [Niujie Mosque](/wiki/Niujie_Mosque "Niujie Mosque"), the oldest mosque in the city.^[\[224\]](#cite_note-230)^^[\[225\]](#cite_note-231)^ The Niujie Mosque was founded in 996 during the Liao dynasty and is frequently visited by Muslim dignitaries. The Chinese Muslim community reportedly celebrated [Ramadan](/wiki/Ramadan "Ramadan") and made [Eid prayers](/wiki/Eid_prayers "Eid prayers") at the mosque in 2021.^[\[226\]](#cite_note-232)^^[\[227\]](#cite_note-233)^{#cite_ref-233}

The largest mosque^[\[228\]](#cite_note-234)^ in Beijing is ChangYing mosque, located in ChaoYang district, with an area of 8,400 square meters.{#cite_ref-234}

Other notable mosques in the old city include the [Dongsi Mosque](/wiki/Dongsi_Mosque "Dongsi Mosque"), founded in 1346; the Huashi Mosque, founded in 1415; Nan Douya Mosque, near Chaoyangmen; Jinshifang Street Mosque, in Xicheng District; and the Dongzhimen Mosque.^[\[229\]](#cite_note-235)^ There are large mosques in outlying Muslim communities in Haidian, [Madian](/wiki/Madian,_Beijing "Madian, Beijing"), Tongzhou, Changping, Changying, Shijingshan and Miyun. The China Islamic Institute is located in the Niujie neighborhood in Xicheng District.{#cite_ref-235}  

### Christianity {#Christianity}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Christianity")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Church_of_the_Saviour%2C_Beijing_5.jpg/220px-Church_of_the_Saviour%2C_Beijing_5.jpg)](/wiki/File:Church_of_the_Saviour,_Beijing_5.jpg) [Church of the Saviour](/wiki/Church_of_the_Saviour,_Beijing "Church of the Saviour, Beijing"), also known as the Xishiku Church, built in 1703  

#### Catholicism {#Catholicism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Catholicism")\]

In 1289, [John of Montecorvino](/wiki/John_of_Montecorvino "John of Montecorvino") came to Beijing as a [Franciscan](/wiki/Franciscan "Franciscan") missionary with the order from the Pope. After meeting and receiving the support of [Kublai Khan](/wiki/Kublai_Khan "Kublai Khan") in 1293, he built the first Catholic church in Beijing in 1305. The [Chinese Patriotic Catholic Association](/wiki/Chinese_Patriotic_Catholic_Association "Chinese Patriotic Catholic Association") (CPCA), based in [Houhai](/wiki/Houhai "Houhai") is the government oversight body for Catholics in mainland China. Notable Catholic churches in Beijing include:

* the Nantang or [Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception](/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Immaculate_Conception,_Beijing "Cathedral of the Immaculate Conception, Beijing") also known as the Xuanwumen Church, which was founded in 1605 and whose current archbishop, [Joseph Li Shan](/wiki/Joseph_Li_Shan "Joseph Li Shan"), is one of the few bishops in China to have the support of both the Vatican and the CPCA.
* the Dongtang or [St. Joseph's Church](/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_Church,_Beijing "St. Joseph's Church, Beijing"), better known as the Wangfujing Church, founded in 1653.
* the Beitang or [Church of the Saviour](/wiki/Church_of_the_Saviour,_Beijing "Church of the Saviour, Beijing"), also known as the Xishiku Church, founded in 1703.
* the Xitang or [Church of Our Lady of Mount Carmel](/wiki/Church_of_Our_Lady_of_Mount_Carmel,_Beijing "Church of Our Lady of Mount Carmel, Beijing") also known as the Xizhimen Church, founded in 1723.

The [National Seminary of Catholic Church in China](/wiki/National_Seminary_of_Catholic_Church_in_China "National Seminary of Catholic Church in China") is located in [Daxing District](/wiki/Daxing_District "Daxing District").
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Haidian_Christian_Church_%2820200906173658%29.jpg/220px-Haidian_Christian_Church_%2820200906173658%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Haidian_Christian_Church_(20200906173658).jpg) [Haidian Christian Church](/wiki/Haidian_Christian_Church "Haidian Christian Church")  

#### Protestantism {#Protestantism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Protestantism")\]

The earliest Protestant churches in Beijing were founded by [British and American missionaries](/wiki/Protestant_missions_in_China_1807%E2%80%931953 "Protestant missions in China 1807–1953") in the second half of the 19th century. Protestant missionaries also opened schools, universities and hospitals which have become important civic institutions. Most of Beijing's Protestant churches were destroyed during the [Boxer Rebellion](/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion "Boxer Rebellion") and afterwards rebuilt. In 1958, the 64 Protestant churches in the city are reorganized into four and overseen by the state through the [Three-Self Patriotic Movement](/wiki/Three-Self_Patriotic_Movement "Three-Self Patriotic Movement").  

#### Eastern Orthodox {#Eastern_Orthodox}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Eastern Orthodox")\]

There was a significant amount of [Orthodox Christians](/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy "Eastern Orthodoxy") in Beijing. Orthodoxy came to Beijing with [Russian prisoners](/wiki/Albazinians "Albazinians") from the [Sino-Russian border conflicts](/wiki/Sino-Russian_border_conflicts "Sino-Russian border conflicts") of the 17th century.^[\[230\]](#cite_note-236)^ In 1956, Viktor, the bishop of Beijing returned to the [Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"), and the Soviet embassy took over the old cathedral and demolished it. In 2007, the Russian embassy built a new church in its garden to serve the Russian Orthodox Christians in Beijing.{#cite_ref-236}  

### Media {#Media}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Media")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/CCTV_Headquarters_5.jpg/180px-CCTV_Headquarters_5.jpg)](/wiki/File:CCTV_Headquarters_5.jpg) The [China Central Television Headquarters building](/wiki/China_Central_Television_Headquarters_building "China Central Television Headquarters building") in the [Beijing CBD](/wiki/Beijing_CBD "Beijing CBD")  

#### Television and radio {#Television_and_radio}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Television and radio")\]

[Beijing Television](/wiki/Beijing_Television "Beijing Television") broadcasts on channels 1 through 10, and [China Central Television](/wiki/China_Central_Television "China Central Television"), China's largest television network, maintains its headquarters in Beijing. Three radio stations feature programmes in English: *Hit FM* on FM 88.7, *Easy FM* by [China Radio International](/wiki/China_Radio_International "China Radio International") on FM 91.5, and the newly launched *Radio 774* on AM 774. [Beijing Radio Stations](/wiki/Beijing_Radio_Stations "Beijing Radio Stations") is the family of radio stations serving the city.  

#### Press {#Press}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Press")\]

The well-known *[Beijing Evening News](/wiki/Beijing_Evening_News "Beijing Evening News")* , covering news about Beijing in Chinese, is distributed every afternoon. Other newspapers include *[Beijing Daily](/wiki/Beijing_Daily "Beijing Daily")* , *[The Beijing News](/wiki/The_Beijing_News "The Beijing News")* , the *[Beijing Star Daily](/wiki/Beijing_Star_Daily "Beijing Star Daily")* , the *Beijing Morning News* , and the *[Beijing Youth Daily](/wiki/Beijing_Youth_Daily "Beijing Youth Daily")* , as well as English-language weeklies *Beijing Weekend* and *[Beijing Today](/wiki/Beijing_Today "Beijing Today")* . The *[People's Daily](/wiki/People%27s_Daily "People's Daily")* , *[Global Times](/wiki/Global_Times "Global Times")* and the *[China Daily](/wiki/China_Daily "China Daily")* (English) are published in Beijing as well.

Publications primarily aimed at international visitors and the expatriate community include the English-language periodicals *Time Out Beijing* , *[City Weekend](/wiki/City_Weekend "City Weekend")* , *[Beijing This Month](/wiki/Beijing_This_Month "Beijing This Month")* , *Beijing Talk* , *[That's Beijing](/wiki/That%27s_Beijing "That's Beijing")* , and *[The Beijinger](/wiki/The_Beijinger "The Beijinger")*.  

#### Beijing rock {#Beijing_rock}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Beijing rock")\]

Beijing rock (Chinese: 北京摇滚) is a wide variety of rock and roll music made by rock bands and solo artists from Beijing. The first rock band in Beijing is [Peking All-Stars](/wiki/Peking_All-Stars "Peking All-Stars"), which was formed in 1979 by foreigners.

Famous rock bands and solo artists from Beijing include [Cui Jian](/wiki/Cui_Jian "Cui Jian"), [Dou Wei](/wiki/Dou_Wei "Dou Wei"), [He Yong](/wiki/He_Yong_(rock_musician) "He Yong (rock musician)"), [Pu Shu](/wiki/Pu_Shu "Pu Shu"), [Tang Dynasty](/wiki/Tang_Dynasty_(band) "Tang Dynasty (band)"), [Black Panther](/wiki/Black_Panther_(band) "Black Panther (band)"), [The Flowers](/wiki/The_Flowers_(Chinese_band) "The Flowers (Chinese band)"), [43 Baojia Street](/wiki/Wang_Feng_(singer) "Wang Feng (singer)"), etc.^[\[231\]](#cite_note-237)^{#cite_ref-237}  

Sports {#Sports}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Sports")\]  
See also: [Football in Beijing](/wiki/Football_in_Beijing "Football in Beijing")  

### Events {#Events}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Events")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg/220px-Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg)](/wiki/File:Beijing_Olympics_2008.jpg) A scene from the opening ceremonies of the [2008 Summer Olympic Games](/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympic_Games "2008 Summer Olympic Games") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/New_Beijing_Workers%27_Stadium%2C_2023.jpg/220px-New_Beijing_Workers%27_Stadium%2C_2023.jpg)](/wiki/File:New_Beijing_Workers%27_Stadium,_2023.jpg) [Beijing Workers' Stadium](/wiki/Beijing_Workers%27_Stadium "Beijing Workers' Stadium")

Beijing has hosted numerous international and national sporting events, the most notables was the [2008 Summer Olympic](/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics "2008 Summer Olympics") and [Paralympic](/wiki/2008_Summer_Paralympics "2008 Summer Paralympics") Games and the [2022 Winter Olympics](/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics "2022 Winter Olympics") and the [Paralympics](/wiki/2022_Winter_Paralympics "2022 Winter Paralympics"). Other [multi-sport](/wiki/Multi-sport_event "Multi-sport event") international events held in Beijing include the [2001 Summer Universiade](/wiki/2001_Summer_Universiade "2001 Summer Universiade") and the [1990 Asian Games](/wiki/1990_Asian_Games "1990 Asian Games"). Single-sport international competitions include the [Beijing Marathon](/wiki/Beijing_Marathon "Beijing Marathon") (annually since 1981), [China Open of Tennis](/wiki/China_Open_(tennis) "China Open (tennis)") (1993--97, annually since 2004), ISU Grand Prix of Figure Skating [Cup of China](/wiki/Cup_of_China "Cup of China") (2003, 2004, 2005, 2008, 2009 and 2010), World Professional Billiards and Snooker Association [China Open for Snooker](/wiki/China_Open_(snooker) "China Open (snooker)") (annually since 2005), Union Cycliste Internationale [Tour of Beijing](/wiki/Tour_of_Beijing "Tour of Beijing") (since [2011](/wiki/2011_Tour_of_Beijing "2011 Tour of Beijing")), 1961 [World Table Tennis Championships](/wiki/World_Table_Tennis_Championships "World Table Tennis Championships"), [1987 IBF Badminton World Championships](/wiki/1987_IBF_World_Championships "1987 IBF World Championships"), the [2004 AFC Asian Cup](/wiki/2004_AFC_Asian_Cup "2004 AFC Asian Cup") (football), and [2009 Barclays Asia Trophy](/wiki/2009_Barclays_Asia_Trophy "2009 Barclays Asia Trophy") (football). Beijing hosted the [2015 IAAF World Championships in Athletics](/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics "2015 World Championships in Athletics").

Beijing's [LeSports Center](/wiki/LeSports_Center "LeSports Center") is one of the main venues for the [2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup](/wiki/2019_FIBA_Basketball_World_Cup "2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup").^[\[232\]](#cite_note-238)^{#cite_ref-238}

The city hosted the second [Chinese National Games](/wiki/National_Games_of_China "National Games of China") in 1914 and the first four [National Games of China](/wiki/National_Games_of_China "National Games of China") in 1959, 1965, 1975, 1979, respectively, and co-hosted the 1993 National Games with [Sichuan](/wiki/Sichuan "Sichuan") and [Qingdao](/wiki/Qingdao "Qingdao"). Beijing also hosted the inaugural [National Peasants' Games](/wiki/National_Peasants%27_Games "National Peasants' Games") in 1988 and the sixth National Minority Games in 1999.

In November 2013, Beijing made a [bid](/wiki/Beijing_bid_for_the_2022_Winter_Olympics "Beijing bid for the 2022 Winter Olympics") to host the [2022 Winter Olympics](/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics "2022 Winter Olympics").^[\[21\]](#cite_note-:2-24)^ On 31 July 2015, the International Olympic Committee awarded the 2022 Winter Olympics to the city becoming the first ever to host both Summer and Winter Olympics also for the [2022 Winter Paralympics](/wiki/2022_Winter_Paralympics "2022 Winter Paralympics") becoming the first ever to host both Summer and Winter Paralympics.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-:3-25)^{#cite_ref-:3_25-1}  

### Venues {#Venues}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Venues")\]

Major sporting venues in the city include the [MasterCard Center](/wiki/MasterCard_Center "MasterCard Center") at [Wukesong](/wiki/Wukesong_station "Wukesong station") west of downtown; the [Workers' Stadium](/wiki/Workers%27_Stadium "Workers' Stadium") and [Workers' Arena](/wiki/Workers_Indoor_Arena "Workers Indoor Arena") in [Sanlitun](/wiki/Sanlitun "Sanlitun") just east of downtown and the [Capital Arena](/wiki/Capital_Indoor_Stadium "Capital Indoor Stadium") in Baishiqiao, northeast of downtown. In addition, many universities in the city have their own sport facilities.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ The [Olympic Green](/wiki/Olympic_Green "Olympic Green") is a stadium cluster centered on the [National Stadium](/wiki/Beijing_National_Stadium "Beijing National Stadium"). It was originally developed for the 2008 Summer Olympics^[\[233\]](#cite_note-239)^ and modified for the 2022 Winter Olympics. The [Big Air Shougang](/wiki/Big_Air_Shougang "Big Air Shougang") ski jump is in the western suburbs and was built for the 2022 Winter Olympics.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-240)^{#cite_ref-240}  

### Clubs {#Clubs}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Clubs")\]

Professional sports teams based in Beijing include:  
* [China Baseball League](/wiki/China_Baseball_League "China Baseball League")
  * [Beijing Tigers](/wiki/Beijing_Tigers "Beijing Tigers")
* [Chinese Basketball Association](/wiki/Chinese_Basketball_Association "Chinese Basketball Association")
  * [Beijing Ducks](/wiki/Beijing_Ducks "Beijing Ducks")
  * [Beijing Royal Fighters](/wiki/Beijing_Royal_Fighters "Beijing Royal Fighters")
* [Women's Chinese Basketball Association](/wiki/Women%27s_Chinese_Basketball_Association "Women's Chinese Basketball Association")
  * Beijing Shougang
* [Kontinental Hockey League](/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League "Kontinental Hockey League")
  * [HC Kunlun Red Star](/wiki/HC_Kunlun_Red_Star "HC Kunlun Red Star")
* [Chinese Super League](/wiki/Chinese_Super_League "Chinese Super League")
  * [Beijing Guoan](/wiki/Beijing_Guoan_F.C. "Beijing Guoan F.C.")
* [China League Two](/wiki/China_League_Two "China League Two")
  * [Beijing BIT](/wiki/Beijing_Institute_of_Technology_F.C. "Beijing Institute of Technology F.C.")
* [Chinese Women's National League](/wiki/Chinese_Women%27s_National_League "Chinese Women's National League")
  * [Beijing BG Phoenix](/wiki/Beijing_BG_Phoenix_F.C. "Beijing BG Phoenix F.C.")

The [Beijing Olympians](/wiki/Beijing_Olympians "Beijing Olympians") of the [American Basketball Association](/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(2000%E2%80%93present) "American Basketball Association (2000–present)"), formerly a [Chinese Basketball Association](/wiki/Chinese_Basketball_Association "Chinese Basketball Association") team, kept their name and maintained a roster of primarily Chinese players after moving to [Maywood, California](/wiki/Maywood,_California "Maywood, California") in 2005.

[China Bandy Federation](/wiki/China_Bandy_Federation "China Bandy Federation") is based in Beijing, one of several cities in which the potential for [bandy](/wiki/Bandy "Bandy") development is explored.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-241)^{#cite_ref-241}  

Transportation {#Transportation}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Transportation")\]  
Main article: [Transport in Beijing](/wiki/Transport_in_Beijing "Transport in Beijing")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Beijing_South_Railway_Station_2094.jpg/220px-Beijing_South_Railway_Station_2094.jpg)](/wiki/File:Beijing_South_Railway_Station_2094.jpg) [Beijing South railway station](/wiki/Beijing_South_railway_station "Beijing South railway station"), one of several in the city

Beijing is an important [transport hub](/wiki/Transport_hub "Transport hub") in [North China](/wiki/North_China "North China") with six [ring roads](/wiki/Ring_roads_of_Beijing "Ring roads of Beijing"), 1167 km (725 miles) of expressways,^[\[236\]](#cite_note-19nj-242)^ 15 National Highways, nine conventional railways, and six high-speed railways converging on the city.{#cite_ref-19nj_242-0}  

### Rail and high-speed rail {#Rail_and_high-speed_rail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Rail and high-speed rail")\]

Beijing serves as a large rail hub in [China's railway network](/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China "Rail transport in the People's Republic of China"). Ten conventional rail lines radiate from the city to: [Shanghai (Jinghu Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Shanghai_railway "Beijing–Shanghai railway"), [Guangzhou (Jingguang Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Guangzhou_railway "Beijing–Guangzhou railway"), [Kowloon (Jingjiu Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Kowloon_railway "Beijing–Kowloon railway"), [Harbin (Jingha Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Harbin_railway "Beijing–Harbin railway") (including [Qinhuangdao (Jingqin Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Qinhuangdao_railway "Beijing–Qinhuangdao railway")), [Baotou (Jingbao Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Baotou_railway "Beijing–Baotou railway"), [Chengde (Jingcheng Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Chengde_railway "Beijing–Chengde railway"), [Tongliao, Inner Mongolia (Jingtong Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Tongliao_railway "Beijing–Tongliao railway"), [Yuanping, Shanxi (Jingyuan Line)](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Yuanping_railway "Beijing–Yuanping railway") and [Shacheng, Hebei (Fengsha Line)](/wiki/Fengtai%E2%80%93Shacheng_railway "Fengtai–Shacheng railway"). In addition, the [Datong--Qinhuangdao railway](/wiki/Datong%E2%80%93Qinhuangdao_railway "Datong–Qinhuangdao railway") passes through the municipality to the north of the city.

Beijing also has six [high-speed rail](/wiki/High-speed_rail "High-speed rail") lines: the [Beijing--Tianjin intercity railway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Tianjin_intercity_railway "Beijing–Tianjin intercity railway"), which opened in 2008; the [Beijing--Shanghai high-speed railway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Shanghai_high-speed_railway "Beijing–Shanghai high-speed railway"), which opened in 2011; the [Beijing--Guangzhou high-speed railway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Guangzhou_high-speed_railway "Beijing–Guangzhou high-speed railway"), which opened in 2012; and the [Beijing--Xiong'an intercity railway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Xiong%27an_intercity_railway "Beijing–Xiong'an intercity railway") and the [Beijing--Zhangjiakou intercity railway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Zhangjiakou_intercity_railway "Beijing–Zhangjiakou intercity railway"), both of which opened in 2019. The [Beijing--Shenyang high-speed railway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Shenyang_high-speed_railway "Beijing–Shenyang high-speed railway") was completed in 2021.

The city's main railway stations are the [Beijing railway station](/wiki/Beijing_railway_station "Beijing railway station"), which opened in 1959; the [Beijing West railway station](/wiki/Beijing_West_railway_station "Beijing West railway station"), which opened in 1996; and the [Beijing South railway station](/wiki/Beijing_South_railway_station "Beijing South railway station"), which was rebuilt into the city's high-speed railway station in 2008; The [Beijing North railway station](/wiki/Beijing_North_railway_station "Beijing North railway station"), was first built in 1905 and expanded in 2009; The [Qinghe railway station](/wiki/Qinghe_railway_station "Qinghe railway station"), was first built in 1905 and expanded in 2019; The [Beijing Chaoyang railway station](/wiki/Beijing_Chaoyang_railway_station "Beijing Chaoyang railway station") opened in 2021; The [Beijing Fengtai railway station](/wiki/Beijing_Fengtai_railway_station "Beijing Fengtai railway station") opened in 2022; and the [Beijing Sub-Center railway station](/wiki/Beijing_Sub-Center_railway_station "Beijing Sub-Center railway station") is under construction.

Smaller stations in the city including [Beijing East railway station](/wiki/Beijing_East_railway_station "Beijing East railway station") and [Daxing Airport station](/wiki/Daxing_Airport_station "Daxing Airport station") handle mainly commuter passenger traffic. In outlying suburbs and counties of Beijing, there are over 40 railway stations.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-243)^{#cite_ref-243}

From Beijing, [direct passenger train service](/wiki/Passenger_rail_transport_in_China "Passenger rail transport in China") is available to most large cities in China. International train service is available to [Mongolia](/wiki/Mongolia "Mongolia"), Russia, [Vietnam](/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam") and [North Korea](/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea"). Passenger trains in China are numbered according to their [direction](/wiki/Railroad_direction "Railroad direction") in relation to Beijing.  

### Roads and expressways {#Roads_and_expressways}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Roads and expressways")\]  
Further information: [Expressways of Beijing](/wiki/Expressways_of_Beijing "Expressways of Beijing") and [China National Highways of Beijing](/wiki/China_National_Highways_of_Beijing "China National Highways of Beijing")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Dongfeng_North_Bridge_%2820210502140735%29.jpg/220px-Dongfeng_North_Bridge_%2820210502140735%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Dongfeng_North_Bridge_(20210502140735).jpg) View of [4th Ring Road](/wiki/4th_Ring_Road "4th Ring Road") in [Chaoyang District](/wiki/Chaoyang_District,_Beijing "Chaoyang District, Beijing")

Beijing is connected by road links to all parts of China as part of the National Trunk Road Network. Many [expressways of China](/wiki/Expressways_of_China "Expressways of China") serve Beijing, as do 15 [China National Highways](/wiki/China_National_Highway "China National Highway"). Beijing's urban transport is dependent upon the [ring roads](/wiki/Ring_Roads_of_Beijing "Ring Roads of Beijing") that concentrically surround the city, with the [Forbidden City](/wiki/Forbidden_City "Forbidden City") area marked as the geographical center for the ring roads. The ring roads appear more rectangular than ring-shaped. There is no official "1st Ring Road". The [2nd Ring Road](/wiki/2nd_Ring_Road "2nd Ring Road") is located in the inner city. Ring roads tend to resemble [expressways](/wiki/Controlled-access_highway "Controlled-access highway") progressively as they extend outwards, with the [5th](/wiki/5th_Ring_Road "5th Ring Road") and [6th Ring Roads](/wiki/6th_Ring_Road "6th Ring Road") being full-standard national expressways, linked to other roads only by interchanges. Expressways to other regions of China are generally accessible from the [3rd Ring Road](/wiki/3rd_Ring_Road_(Beijing) "3rd Ring Road (Beijing)") outward. A final outer orbital, the [Capital Area Loop Expressway (G95)](/wiki/G95_Capital_Area_Loop_Expressway "G95 Capital Area Loop Expressway"), was fully opened in 2018 and will extend into neighboring [Tianjin](/wiki/Tianjin "Tianjin") and [Hebei](/wiki/Hebei "Hebei").
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Jingtong_Expwy_east_of_Sihui_%2820230828160357%29.jpg/220px-Jingtong_Expwy_east_of_Sihui_%2820230828160357%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Jingtong_Expwy_east_of_Sihui_(20230828160357).jpg) [Beijing--Tongzhou Expressway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Tongzhou_Expressway "Beijing–Tongzhou Expressway")

Within the urban core, city streets generally follow the checkerboard pattern of the ancient capital. Many of Beijing's boulevards and streets with "inner" and "outer" are still named in relation to gates in the city wall, though most gates no longer stand. Traffic jams are a major concern. Even outside of rush hour, several roads still remain clogged with traffic.

Beijing's urban design layout further exacerbates transportation problems.^[\[238\]](#cite_note-244)^ The authorities have introduced several bus lanes, which only public buses can use during rush hour. In the beginning of 2010, Beijing had 4 million registered automobiles.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-245)^ By the end of 2010, the government forecast 5 million. In 2010, new car registrations in Beijing averaged 15,500 per week.^[\[240\]](#cite_note-246)^{#cite_ref-246}

Towards the end of 2010, the city government announced a series of drastic measures to tackle traffic jams, including limiting the number of new license plates issued to passenger cars to 20,000 a month and barring cars with non-Beijing plates from entering areas within the Fifth Ring Road during rush hour.^[\[241\]](#cite_note-247)^ More restrictive measures are also reserved during major events or heavily polluted weather.{#cite_ref-247}

To obtain a valid license plate, Beijing drivers must be selected in a lottery.^[\[122\]](#cite_note-:03-127)^^: 168^ As part of government policy support for the use of electric vehicles, Beijing drivers with fully electric cars have a much greater chance of being selected for a license plate.^[\[122\]](#cite_note-:03-127)^^: 168^ Additionally, fully electric vehicles are exempt from restrictions on which day of the week a driver may drive their vehicle.^[\[122\]](#cite_note-:03-127)^^: 168^{#cite_ref-:03_127-3}

Road signs began to be standardized with both Chinese and English names displayed, with location names using pinyin, in 2008.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-248)^{#cite_ref-248}  

### Air {#Air}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Air")\]  

#### Beijing Capital International Airport {#Beijing_Capital_International_Airport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Beijing Capital International Airport")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Air_China_first_and_business_lounge_at_ZBAA_T3C_%2820170309125425%29.jpg/220px-Air_China_first_and_business_lounge_at_ZBAA_T3C_%2820170309125425%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Air_China_first_and_business_lounge_at_ZBAA_T3C_(20170309125425).jpg) Terminal 3 of the [Beijing Capital International Airport](/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport "Beijing Capital International Airport")

Beijing has two of the world's largest airports. The [Beijing Capital International Airport](/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport "Beijing Capital International Airport") ([IATA](/wiki/IATA "IATA"): PEK) located 32 kilometres (20 mi) northeast of the city center in [Chaoyang District](/wiki/Chaoyang_District,_Beijing "Chaoyang District, Beijing") bordering [Shunyi District](/wiki/Shunyi_District "Shunyi District"), is the [second busiest airport in the world](/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic "World's busiest airports by passenger traffic") after [Atlanta](/wiki/Atlanta "Atlanta")'s [Hartsfield--Jackson International Airport](/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport "Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport").^[\[17\]](#cite_note-ACI_aero-20)^ Capital Airport's Terminal 3, built during the expansion for the 2008 Olympics, is one of the largest in the world. Capital Airport is the main hub for [Air China](/wiki/Air_China "Air China") and [Hainan Airlines](/wiki/Hainan_Airlines "Hainan Airlines"). The [Airport Expressway](/wiki/Airport_Expressway_(Beijing) "Airport Expressway (Beijing)") and [Second Airport Expressway](/wiki/2nd_Airport_Expressway "2nd Airport Expressway"), connect to Capital Airport from the northeast and east of the city center, respectively. Driving time from city center is about 40 minutes under normal traffic conditions. The [Capital Airport Express](/wiki/Capital_Airport_Express "Capital Airport Express") line of [Beijing Subway](/wiki/Beijing_Subway "Beijing Subway") and the [Capital Airport Bus](/wiki/Beijing_Airport_Bus "Beijing Airport Bus") serves the Capital Airport.{#cite_ref-ACI_aero_20-1}  

#### Beijing Daxing International Airport {#Beijing_Daxing_International_Airport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Beijing Daxing International Airport")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Beijing_Daxing_International_Airport_13.jpg/220px-Beijing_Daxing_International_Airport_13.jpg)](/wiki/File:Beijing_Daxing_International_Airport_13.jpg) [Beijing Daxing International Airport](/wiki/Beijing_Daxing_International_Airport "Beijing Daxing International Airport")

The [Beijing Daxing International Airport](/wiki/Beijing_Daxing_International_Airport "Beijing Daxing International Airport") (IATA: PKX) located 46 kilometres (29 mi) south of the city in [Daxing District](/wiki/Daxing_District "Daxing District") bordering the city of [Langfang](/wiki/Langfang "Langfang"), [Hebei Province](/wiki/Hebei_Province "Hebei Province"), opened on 25 September 2019.^[\[243\]](#cite_note-249)^^[\[244\]](#cite_note-carnoc20160112-250)^^[\[245\]](#cite_note-251)^ The Daxing Airport has one of the world's largest terminal buildings and is expected to be a major airport serving Beijing, Tianjin and northern Hebei Province. Daxing Airport is connected to the city via the [Beijing--Xiong'an intercity railway](/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Xiong%27an_intercity_railway "Beijing–Xiong'an intercity railway"), the [Daxing Airport Express](/wiki/Daxing_Airport_Express "Daxing Airport Express") line of the Beijing Subway and two expressways.{#cite_ref-251}  

#### Other airports {#Other_airports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Other airports")\]

With the opening of the Daxing Airport in September 2019, the [Beijing Nanyuan Airport](/wiki/Beijing_Nanyuan_Airport "Beijing Nanyuan Airport") (IATA: NAY), located 13 kilometres (8.1 mi) south of center in [Fengtai District](/wiki/Fengtai_District "Fengtai District"), has been closed to civilian airline service. Other airports in the city at Liangxiang, Xijiao, Shahe and Badaling are primarily for military use.  

#### Visa requirements for air passengers {#Visa_requirements_for_air_passengers}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=52 "Edit section: Visa requirements for air passengers")\]

As of 1 January 2013^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit)^, tourists from 45 countries are permitted a 72-hour visa-free stay in Beijing. The 45 countries include Singapore, Japan, the United States, Canada, all EU and EEA countries (except Norway and Liechtenstein), Switzerland, Brazil, Argentina and Australia. The programme benefits transit and business travellers^[\[246\]](#cite_note-252)^ with the 72 hours calculated starting from the moment visitors receive their transit stay permits rather than the time of their plane's arrival. Foreign visitors are not permitted to leave Beijing for other Chinese cities during the 72 hours.^[\[247\]](#cite_note-Beijing-253)^{#cite_ref-Beijing_253-0}  

### Public transit {#Public_transit}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Public transit")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Train_leaving_Xihongmen_Station.JPG/220px-Train_leaving_Xihongmen_Station.JPG)](/wiki/File:Train_leaving_Xihongmen_Station.JPG) A [Daxing line](/wiki/Daxing_line "Daxing line") train on the [Beijing Subway](/wiki/Beijing_Subway "Beijing Subway"), which is among the longest and busiest [rapid transit](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") systems in the world [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/4838397_at_Tian%27anmen_%2820200825105132%29.jpg/220px-4838397_at_Tian%27anmen_%2820200825105132%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:4838397_at_Tian%27anmen_(20200825105132).jpg) An articulated [Beijing bus](/wiki/Beijing_bus "Beijing bus")

The [Beijing Subway](/wiki/Beijing_Subway "Beijing Subway"), which began operating in 1969, now has 25 lines, 459 [stations](/wiki/List_of_Beijing_Subway_stations "List of Beijing Subway stations"), and 783 km (487 mi) of [lines](/wiki/Line_length "Line length"). It is the [longest subway system in the world](/wiki/List_of_metro_systems "List of metro systems") and [first in annual ridership](/wiki/Metro_systems_by_annual_passenger_rides "Metro systems by annual passenger rides") with 3.66 billion rides delivered in 2016. In 2013, with a flat fare of [¥](/wiki/Renminbi "Renminbi")2.00 (US$0.31) per ride with unlimited transfers on all lines except the [Airport Express](/wiki/Airport_Express,_Beijing_Subway "Airport Express, Beijing Subway"), the subway was also the most affordable [rapid transit system in China](/wiki/Rapid_transit_in_China "Rapid transit in China"). The subway is undergoing rapid expansion and is expected to reach 30 lines, 450 stations, 1,050 kilometres (650 mi) in length by 2022. When fully implemented, 95% of residents inside the [Fourth Ring Road](/wiki/4th_Ring_Road "4th Ring Road") will be able to walk to a station in 15 minutes.^[\[248\]](#cite_note-254)^^\[*[better source needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")*\]^ The [Beijing Suburban Railway](/wiki/Beijing_Suburban_Railway "Beijing Suburban Railway") provides commuter rail service to outlying suburbs of the municipality.{#cite_ref-254}

As part of the urban re-development for the 2008 Olympics, Beijing's subway system was significantly expanded.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-:02-83)^^: 137^ On 28 December 2014, it switched to a distance-based fare system from a fixed fare for all lines except the [Airport Express](/wiki/Airport_Express,_Beijing_Subway "Airport Express, Beijing Subway").^[\[249\]](#cite_note-english.cri.cn-255)^ Under the new system a trip under
6 km (3+1⁄2 mi) will cost [¥](/wiki/Renminbi "Renminbi")3.00(US$0.49), an additional [¥](/wiki/Renminbi "Renminbi")1.00 will be added for the next
6 km (3+1⁄2 mi) and the next 10 km (6 mi) until the distance for the trip reaches 32 km (20 mi).^[\[249\]](#cite_note-english.cri.cn-255)^ For every 20 kilometres (12 miles) after the original 32 kilometres (20 miles) an additional [¥](/wiki/Renminbi "Renminbi")1.00 is added.^[\[249\]](#cite_note-english.cri.cn-255)^ For example, a 50-kilometre (31-mile) trip would cost [¥](/wiki/Renminbi "Renminbi") 8.00.{#cite_ref-english.cri.cn_255-2}

There are nearly 1,000 [public bus](/wiki/Beijing_Bus "Beijing Bus") and [trolleybus](/wiki/Trolleybus "Trolleybus") lines in the city, including four [bus rapid transit](/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit "Bus rapid transit") lines. Standard bus fares are as low as ¥1.00 when purchased with the *[Yikatong](/wiki/Yikatong "Yikatong")* metrocard.  

### Taxi {#Taxi}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=54 "Edit section: Taxi")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Beijing_EU5_Taxis_IMG001.jpg/220px-Beijing_EU5_Taxis_IMG001.jpg)](/wiki/File:Beijing_EU5_Taxis_IMG001.jpg) Beijing EU5 Taxi in Beijing

Metered [taxi](/wiki/Taxicab "Taxicab") in Beijing start at ¥13 for the first 3 kilometres (1.9 mi), ¥2.3 [Renminbi](/wiki/Renminbi "Renminbi") per additional 1 kilometre (0.62 mi) and ¥1 per ride fuel surcharge, not counting idling fees which are ¥2.3 (¥4.6 during rush hours of 7--9 am and 5--7 pm) per 5 minutes of standing or running at speeds lower than 12 kilometres per hour (7.5 mph). Most taxis are [Hyundai Elantras](/wiki/Hyundai_Elantra "Hyundai Elantra"), [Hyundai Sonatas](/wiki/Hyundai_Sonata "Hyundai Sonata"), [Peugeots](/wiki/Peugeot "Peugeot"), [Citroëns](/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn "Citroën") and [Volkswagen Jettas](/wiki/Volkswagen_Jetta "Volkswagen Jetta"). After 15 kilometres (9.3 mi), the base fare increases by 50% (but is only applied to the portion *over* that distance). Different companies have special colours combinations painted on their vehicles. Usually registered taxis have yellowish brown as basic hue, with another color of Prussian blue, hunter green, white, umber, tyrian purple, rufous, or sea green. Between 11 pm and 5 am, there is also a 20% fee increase. Rides over 15 km (9 mi) and between 23:00 and 06:00 incur both charges, for a total increase of 80%. Tolls during trip should be covered by customers and the costs of trips beyond Beijing city limits should be negotiated with the driver. The cost of unregistered taxis is also subject to negotiation with the driver.  

### Bicycles {#Bicycles}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=55 "Edit section: Bicycles")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/East_start_of_Huilongguan-Shangdi_Bicycle_Lane_%2820190607134646%29.jpg/220px-East_start_of_Huilongguan-Shangdi_Bicycle_Lane_%2820190607134646%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:East_start_of_Huilongguan-Shangdi_Bicycle_Lane_(20190607134646).jpg) Huilongguan--Shangdi bicycle lane

Beijing has long been well known for the number of bicycles on its streets. Although the rise of motor traffic has created a great deal of congestion and bicycle use has declined, bicycles are still an important form of local transportation. Many cyclists can be seen on most roads in the city, and most of the main roads have dedicated [bicycle lanes](/wiki/Bicycle_lanes "Bicycle lanes"). Beijing is relatively flat, which makes cycling convenient. The rise of [electric bicycles](/wiki/Electric_bicycles "Electric bicycles") and [electric scooters](/wiki/Electric_scooters "Electric scooters"), which have similar speeds and use the same cycle lanes, may have brought about a revival in bicycle-speed two-wheeled transport. It is possible to cycle to most parts of the city. Because of the growing traffic congestion, the authorities have indicated more than once that they wish to encourage cycling, but it is not clear whether there is sufficient will to translate that into action on a significant scale.^[\[250\]](#cite_note-256)^ On 30 March 2019, a 6.5 km (4 mile) bicycle-dedicated lane was opened, easing the traffic congestion between [Huilongguan](/wiki/Huilongguan "Huilongguan") and [Shangdi](/wiki/Shangdi "Shangdi") where there are many high-tech companies.^[\[251\]](#cite_note-257)^ Cycling has seen a resurgence in popularity spurred by the emergence of a large number of dockless app based [bikeshares](/wiki/Bicycle-sharing_system "Bicycle-sharing system") such as [Mobike](/wiki/Mobike "Mobike"), [Bluegogo](/wiki/Bluegogo "Bluegogo") and [Ofo](/wiki/Ofo_(bike_sharing) "Ofo (bike sharing)") since 2016.^[\[252\]](#cite_note-258)^{#cite_ref-258}  

Defence and aerospace {#Defence_and_aerospace}
----------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=56 "Edit section: Defence and aerospace")\]

|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg) | This section **does not [cite](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources") any [sources](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")** . Please help [improve this section](/wiki/Special:EditPage/Beijing "Special:EditPage/Beijing") by [adding citations to reliable sources](/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners "Help:Referencing for beginners"). Unsourced material may be challenged and [removed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence "Wikipedia:Verifiability"). *(December 2024)**([Learn how and when to remove this message](/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal "Help:Maintenance template removal"))* |

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Starting_aerial_formation_of_PRC70_Parade_%2820191001112401%29.jpg/240px-Starting_aerial_formation_of_PRC70_Parade_%2820191001112401%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Starting_aerial_formation_of_PRC70_Parade_(20191001112401).jpg) [KJ-2000](/wiki/KJ-2000 "KJ-2000") and [J-10s](/wiki/Chengdu_J-10 "Chengdu J-10") started the [flypast](/wiki/Flypast "Flypast") formation for the [70th anniversary of the People's Republic of China](/wiki/70th_anniversary_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China "70th anniversary of the People's Republic of China").

The command headquarters of China's military forces are based in Beijing. The [Central Military Commission](/wiki/Central_Military_Commission_(China) "Central Military Commission (China)"), the political organ in charge of the military, is housed inside the [Ministry of National Defense](/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defense_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China "Ministry of National Defense of the People's Republic of China"), located next to the [Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution](/wiki/Military_Museum_of_the_Chinese_People%27s_Revolution "Military Museum of the Chinese People's Revolution") in western Beijing. The [Rocket Force](/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Rocket_Force "People's Liberation Army Rocket Force"), which controls the country's [strategic missile](/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile "Intercontinental ballistic missile") and nuclear weapons, has its command in [Qinghe](/wiki/Qinghe_Subdistrict,_Beijing "Qinghe Subdistrict, Beijing"), Haidian District. The headquarters of the [Central Theater Command](/wiki/Central_Theater_Command "Central Theater Command"), one of five nationally, is based further west in Gaojing. The CTR oversees the Beijing Capital Garrison as well as the [81st](/wiki/81st_Army_(People%27s_Republic_of_China) "81st Army (People's Republic of China)"), [82nd](/wiki/82nd_Army_(People%27s_Republic_of_China) "82nd Army (People's Republic of China)") and [83rd Armies](/wiki/83rd_Army_(People%27s_Republic_of_China) "83rd Army (People's Republic of China)"), which are based in Hebei.

Military institutions in Beijing also include academies and thinktanks such as the [PLA National Defence University](/wiki/PLA_National_Defence_University "PLA National Defence University") and [Academy of Military Science](/wiki/PLA_Academy_of_Military_Science "PLA Academy of Military Science"), military hospitals such as the [301](/wiki/301_Military_Hospital "301 Military Hospital"), [307](/wiki/307_Hospital "307 Hospital") and the Academy of Military Medical Sciences, and army-affiliated cultural entities such as 1 August Film Studios and the [PLA Song and Dance Troupe](/wiki/Chinese_People%27s_Liberation_Army_Naval_Song_and_Dance_Troupe "Chinese People's Liberation Army Naval Song and Dance Troupe").

The [China National Space Administration](/wiki/China_National_Space_Administration "China National Space Administration"), which oversees country's [space program](/wiki/Chinese_space_program "Chinese space program"), and several space-related state owned companies, such as [CASTC](/wiki/China_Aerospace_Science_and_Technology_Corporation "China Aerospace Science and Technology Corporation") and [CASIC](/wiki/China_Aerospace_Science_and_Industry_Corporation "China Aerospace Science and Industry Corporation"), are all based in Beijing. The [Beijing Aerospace Command and Control Center](/wiki/Beijing_Aerospace_Command_and_Control_Center "Beijing Aerospace Command and Control Center"), in Haidian District, tracks the country's [crewed](/wiki/Shenzhou_program "Shenzhou program") and uncrewed flight and other space exploration initiatives.  

Nature and wildlife {#Nature_and_wildlife}
------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=57 "Edit section: Nature and wildlife")\]

Beijing Municipality has 20 nature reserves, with a combined area of 1,339.7 km^2^ (517.3 sq mi).^[\[253\]](#cite_note-259)^ The mountains to the west and north of the city are home to a number of protected wildlife species including [leopard](/wiki/Leopard "Leopard"), [leopard cat](/wiki/Leopard_cat "Leopard cat"), [wolf](/wiki/Wolf "Wolf"), [red fox](/wiki/Red_fox "Red fox"), [wild boar](/wiki/Wild_boar "Wild boar"), [masked palm civet](/wiki/Masked_palm_civet "Masked palm civet"), [raccoon dog](/wiki/Raccoon_dog "Raccoon dog"), [hog badger](/wiki/Hog_badger "Hog badger"), [Siberian weasel](/wiki/Siberian_weasel "Siberian weasel"), [Amur hedgehog](/wiki/Amur_hedgehog "Amur hedgehog"), [roe deer](/wiki/Roe_deer "Roe deer"), and [mandarin rat snake](/wiki/Mandarin_rat_snake "Mandarin rat snake").^[\[254\]](#cite_note-260)^^[\[255\]](#cite_note-261)^^[\[256\]](#cite_note-262)^ The Beijing Aquatic Wildlife Rescue and Conservation Center protects the [Chinese giant salamander](/wiki/Chinese_giant_salamander "Chinese giant salamander"), [Amur stickleback](/wiki/Amur_stickleback "Amur stickleback"), and [mandarin duck](/wiki/Mandarin_duck "Mandarin duck") on the Huaijiu and Huaisha Rivers in [Huairou District](/wiki/Huairou_District "Huairou District").^[\[257\]](#cite_note-263)^ To the south of the city, the [Beijing Milu Park](/wiki/Milu_Yuan "Milu Yuan") is home to one of the largest herds of [Père David's deer](/wiki/P%C3%A8re_David%27s_deer "Père David's deer"), which are now extinct in the wild. [Endemic](/wiki/Endemic "Endemic") to Beijing is the [Beijing barbastelle](/wiki/Beijing_barbastelle "Beijing barbastelle"), a species of [vesper bat](/wiki/Vesper_bat "Vesper bat") discovered in caves of [Fangshan District](/wiki/Fangshan_District "Fangshan District") in 2001 and identified as a distinct species in 2007. The mountains of Fangshan are also the natural habitat for the more common [Beijing mouse-eared bat](/wiki/Beijing_mouse-eared_bat "Beijing mouse-eared bat"), [large myotis](/wiki/Large_myotis "Large myotis"), [greater horseshoe bat](/wiki/Greater_horseshoe_bat "Greater horseshoe bat"), and [Rickett's big-footed bat](/wiki/Rickett%27s_big-footed_bat "Rickett's big-footed bat").^[\[258\]](#cite_note-264)^{#cite_ref-264}

Each year, Beijing hosts 200--300 species of [migratory birds](/wiki/Migratory_birds "Migratory birds") including the [common crane](/wiki/Common_crane "Common crane"), [black-headed gull](/wiki/Black-headed_gull "Black-headed gull"), [swan](/wiki/Swan "Swan"), [mallard](/wiki/Mallard "Mallard"), [common cuckoo](/wiki/Common_cuckoo "Common cuckoo"), and the endangered [yellow-breasted bunting](/wiki/Yellow-breasted_bunting "Yellow-breasted bunting").^[\[259\]](#cite_note-265)^^[\[260\]](#cite_note-BJ_Evening_News_2016-10-30-266)^ In May 2016, Common cuckoos nesting in the wetlands of Cuihu (Haidian), Hanshiqiao (Shunyi), Yeyahu (Yanqing) were tagged and have been traced as far as India, Kenya and [Mozambique](/wiki/Mozambique "Mozambique").^[\[261\]](#cite_note-267)^^[\[262\]](#cite_note-268)^ In the fall of 2016, the Beijing Forest Police undertook a month-long campaign to crack down on illegal hunting and trapping of migratory birds for sale in local bird markets.^[\[260\]](#cite_note-BJ_Evening_News_2016-10-30-266)^ Over 1,000 rescued birds of protected species including [streptopelia](/wiki/Streptopelia "Streptopelia"), [Eurasian siskin](/wiki/Eurasian_siskin "Eurasian siskin"), [crested myna](/wiki/Crested_myna "Crested myna"), [coal tit](/wiki/Coal_tit "Coal tit"), and [great tit](/wiki/Great_tit "Great tit") were handed to the Beijing Wildlife Protection and Rescue Center for repatriation to the wild.^[\[260\]](#cite_note-BJ_Evening_News_2016-10-30-266)^^[\[263\]](#cite_note-269)^{#cite_ref-269}

The city flowers are the [Chinese rose](/wiki/Rosa_chinensis "Rosa chinensis") and [chrysanthemum](/wiki/Chrysanthemum "Chrysanthemum").^[\[264\]](#cite_note-cityflowertree-270)^ The city trees are the [Chinese arborvitae](/wiki/Chinese_arborvitae "Chinese arborvitae") (an [evergreen](/wiki/Evergreen "Evergreen") in the [cypress family](/wiki/Cypress_family "Cypress family")) and the [pagoda tree](/wiki/Pagoda_tree "Pagoda tree") (a [deciduous](/wiki/Deciduous "Deciduous") tree in the [bean family](/wiki/Bean_family "Bean family"), also called the Chinese scholar tree).^[\[264\]](#cite_note-cityflowertree-270)^ The oldest scholar tree in the city was planted in what is now [Beihai Park](/wiki/Beihai_Park "Beihai Park") during the [Tang dynasty](/wiki/Tang_dynasty "Tang dynasty").^[\[265\]](#cite_note-271)^{#cite_ref-271}  

International relations {#International_relations}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=58 "Edit section: International relations")\]

The capital is the home of the [Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank](/wiki/Asian_Infrastructure_Investment_Bank "Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank"), a [multilateral development bank](/wiki/Multilateral_development_bank "Multilateral development bank") that aims to improve economic and social outcomes in Asia^[\[266\]](#cite_note-272)^ and the [Silk Road Fund](/wiki/Silk_Road_Fund "Silk Road Fund"), an investment fund of the Chinese government to foster increased investment and provide financial supports in countries along the [One Belt, One Road](/wiki/One_Belt,_One_Road "One Belt, One Road").^[\[267\]](#cite_note-273)^ Beijing is also home to the headquarters of the [Shanghai Cooperation Organisation](/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation "Shanghai Cooperation Organisation") (SCO),^[\[268\]](#cite_note-274)^ making it an important city for [international diplomacy](/wiki/Diplomacy "Diplomacy").{#cite_ref-274}

### Foreign embassies and consulates {#Foreign_embassies_and_consulates}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit&section=60 "Edit section: Foreign embassies and consulates")\]  
See also: [List of diplomatic missions in China](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_China "List of diplomatic missions in China")

In 2019, China had the largest [diplomatic network](/wiki/Diplomatic_mission "Diplomatic mission") in the world.^[\[270\]](#cite_note-276)^ China hosts a [large diplomatic community](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_China "List of diplomatic missions in China") in its capital city of Beijing; as of 2020^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Beijing&action=edit)^, the Chinese capital hosts 173 embassies, one consulate and three representatives, excluding the [trade offices](/wiki/Trade_office "Trade office") of [Hong Kong](/wiki/Hong_Kong "Hong Kong") and [Macau](/wiki/Macau "Macau").^[\[271\]](#cite_note-277)^^[\[272\]](#cite_note-278)^
